<p><b>Colorado</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="/ɒ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;body&#39;">ɒ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ə/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/æ/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;bad&#39;">æ</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span><span title="&#39;d&#39; in &#39;dye&#39;">d</span><span title="/oʊ/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">oʊ</span></span>/</a></span>&#32;<span class="noprint"><span class="ext-phonos"><span data-nosnippet="" id="ooui-php-1" class="ext-phonos-PhonosButton noexcerpt ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel oo-ui-widget oo-ui-widget-enabled oo-ui-buttonElement oo-ui-buttonElement-frameless oo-ui-iconElement oo-ui-buttonWidget" data-ooui="{&quot;_&quot;:&quot;mw.Phonos.PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;href&quot;:&quot;\/\/upload.wikimedia.org\/wikipedia\/commons\/transcoded\/7\/7f\/ColoradanColorado.ogg\/ColoradanColorado.ogg.mp3&quot;,&quot;rel&quot;:[&quot;nofollow&quot;],&quot;framed&quot;:false,&quot;icon&quot;:&quot;volumeUp&quot;,&quot;data&quot;:{&quot;ipa&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;text&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;lang&quot;:&quot;en&quot;,&quot;wikibase&quot;:&quot;&quot;,&quot;file&quot;:&quot;ColoradanColorado.ogg&quot;},&quot;classes&quot;:[&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton&quot;,&quot;noexcerpt&quot;,&quot;ext-phonos-PhonosButton-emptylabel&quot;]}"><a role="button" tabindex="0" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/7/7f/ColoradanColorado.ogg/ColoradanColorado.ogg.mp3" rel="nofollow" aria-label="Play audio" title="Play audio" class="oo-ui-buttonElement-button"><span class="oo-ui-iconElement-icon oo-ui-icon-volumeUp"></span><span class="oo-ui-labelElement-label"></span><span class="oo-ui-indicatorElement-indicator oo-ui-indicatorElement-noIndicator"></span></a></span><sup class="ext-phonos-attribution noexcerpt navigation-not-searchable"><a href="/wiki/File:ColoradanColorado.ogg" title="File:ColoradanColorado.ogg">ⓘ</a></sup></span></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">KOL</span>-ə-<span style="font-size:90%">RAD</span>-oh, -&#8288;<span style="font-size:90%">RAH</span>-doh</i></a>,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> other variants<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>) is a landlocked <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_states" title="Mountain states">Mountain West</a> subregion of the <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">Western</a> <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>. Colorado borders <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Nebraska" title="Nebraska">Nebraska</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a> to the southeast, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> to the south, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> to the west, and meets <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> to the southwest at the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners" title="Four Corners">Four Corners</a>. Colorado is noted for its landscape of <a href="/wiki/Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountains">mountains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Forests">forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">high plains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesas" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesas">mesas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canyons" class="mw-redirect" title="Canyons">canyons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plateaus" class="mw-redirect" title="Plateaus">plateaus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rivers" class="mw-redirect" title="Rivers">rivers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a> lands. Colorado is one of the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_states" title="Mountain states">Mountain States</a> and is often considered to be part of the <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">southwestern United States</a>. The high plains of Colorado may be considered a part of the <a href="/wiki/Midwestern_United_States" title="Midwestern United States">midwestern United States</a>. It encompasses most of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a>, as well as the northeastern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a> and the western edge of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a>. Colorado is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_area" title="List of U.S. states and territories by area">eighth most extensive</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_and_territories_by_population" title="List of U.S. states and territories by population">21st most populous</a> U.S. state. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimated the population of Colorado at 5,877,610 as of July 1, 2023, a 1.80% increase since the 2020 United States census.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The region has been inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native Americans</a> and their <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">ancestors</a> for at least 13,500 years and possibly much longer. The eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> was a major migration route for early peoples who spread throughout the Americas. In 1848, much of the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">Nuevo México</a> region was annexed to the United States with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Pike%27s_Peak_Gold_Rush" class="mw-redirect" title="Pike&#39;s Peak Gold Rush">Pike's Peak Gold Rush</a> of 1858–1862 created an influx of settlers. On February 28, 1861, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/James_Buchanan" title="James Buchanan">James Buchanan</a> signed <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Organic_Act" title="Colorado Organic Act">an act</a> creating the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ColoradoOrganicAct_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoOrganicAct-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and on August 1, 1876, President <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a> signed <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Statehood_Proclamation" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado Statehood Proclamation">Proclamation 230</a> admitting Colorado to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> as the 38th state.<sup id="cite_ref-ColoradoStatehoodProclamation_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoStatehoodProclamation-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> The Spanish adjective <i>"colorado"</i> means "colored red" or "ruddy". Colorado is nicknamed the "<a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_nicknames" class="mw-redirect" title="List of U.S. state nicknames">Centennial State</a>" because it became a state one century (and four weeks) after the signing of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">United States Declaration of Independence</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> is the capital, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_municipalities_by_population" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado municipalities by population">most populous city</a>, and the center of the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>. <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">Colorado Springs</a> is the second most populous city of the state. Residents of the state are known as <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Colorado" title="List of people from Colorado">Coloradans</a>, although the antiquated "Coloradoan" is occasionally used.<sup id="cite_ref-statestyle_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statestyle-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Coloradan_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Coloradan-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Major parts of the <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Colorado" title="Economy of Colorado">economy</a> include government and defense, mining, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Colorado#Agriculture" title="Economy of Colorado">agriculture</a>, tourism, and increasingly other kinds of manufacturing. With increasing temperatures and decreasing water availability, Colorado's agriculture, forestry, and tourism economies are <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Colorado" title="Climate change in Colorado">expected to be heavily affected by climate change</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prehistory_of_Colorado" title="Prehistory of Colorado">Prehistory of Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Colorado" title="History of Colorado">History of Colorado</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For a chronological guide, see <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Colorado_history" title="Timeline of Colorado history">Timeline of Colorado history</a>.</div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg/220px-Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg/330px-Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg/440px-Mesa-Verde---Cliff-Palace-in_1891_-_edit1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2126" data-file-height="1543" /></a><figcaption>The ruins of the <a href="/wiki/Cliff_Palace" title="Cliff Palace">Cliff Palace</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mesa_Verde_National_Park" title="Mesa Verde National Park">Mesa Verde</a>, photographed by <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_Nordenski%C3%B6ld" title="Gustaf Nordenskiöld">Gustaf Nordenskiöld</a> in 1891</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:BentsFort.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BentsFort.jpg/220px-BentsFort.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BentsFort.jpg/330px-BentsFort.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/BentsFort.jpg/440px-BentsFort.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1472" data-file-height="966" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Bent%27s_Old_Fort_National_Historic_Site" title="Bent&#39;s Old Fort National Historic Site">Bent's Old Fort National Historic Site</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_National_Historic_Trail" class="mw-redirect" title="Santa Fe National Historic Trail">Santa Fe National Historic Trail</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The region that is today the State of Colorado has been inhabited by <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Native Americans</a> and their <a href="/wiki/Paleo-Indians" title="Paleo-Indians">Paleoamerican ancestors</a> for at least 13,500 years and possibly more than 37,000 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Footprints_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Footprints-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mammoth_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mammoth-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The eastern edge of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> was a major migration route that was important to the spread of early peoples throughout the Americas. The <a href="/wiki/Lindenmeier_site" title="Lindenmeier site">Lindenmeier site</a> in <a href="/wiki/Larimer_County,_Colorado" title="Larimer County, Colorado">Larimer County</a> contains artifacts dating from approximately 8720 BCE. The <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Pueblo_peoples" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Pueblo peoples">Ancient Pueblo peoples</a> lived in the valleys and mesas of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a> in far southwestern Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ute_Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ute Nation">Ute Nation</a> inhabited the mountain valleys of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Rocky_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Western Rocky Mountains">Western Rocky Mountains</a>, even as far east as the Front Range of the present day. The <a href="/wiki/Apache" title="Apache">Apache</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Comanche" title="Comanche">Comanche</a> also inhabited the Eastern and Southeastern parts of the state. In the 17th century, the <a href="/wiki/Arapaho_Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Arapaho Nation">Arapaho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Cheyenne Nation">Cheyenne</a> moved west from the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region" title="Great Lakes region">Great Lakes region</a> to hunt across the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a> of Colorado and <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> claimed Colorado as part of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_de_Nuevo_M%C3%A9xico" title="Santa Fe de Nuevo México">Nuevo México</a>. The U.S. acquired the territorial claim to the eastern Rocky Mountains with the <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_Purchase" title="Louisiana Purchase">Louisiana Purchase</a> from France in 1803. This U.S. claim conflicted with the claim by Spain to the upper <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_River" title="Arkansas River">Arkansas River Basin</a>. In 1806, <a href="/wiki/Zebulon_Pike" title="Zebulon Pike">Zebulon Pike</a> led a <a href="/wiki/Pike_Expedition" title="Pike Expedition">U.S. Army reconnaissance expedition</a> into the disputed region. Colonel Pike and his troops were arrested by Spanish cavalrymen in the <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Valley" title="San Luis Valley">San Luis Valley</a> the following February, taken to <a href="/wiki/Chihuahua,_Chihuahua" class="mw-redirect" title="Chihuahua, Chihuahua">Chihuahua</a>, and expelled from Mexico the following July.
</p><p>The U.S. relinquished its claim to all land south and west of the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_River" title="Arkansas River">Arkansas River</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/42nd_parallel_north" title="42nd parallel north">42nd parallel north</a> and west of the <a href="/wiki/100th_meridian_west" title="100th meridian west">100th meridian west</a> as part of its purchase of Florida from Spain with the <a href="/wiki/Adams-On%C3%ADs_Treaty" class="mw-redirect" title="Adams-Onís Treaty">Adams-Onís Treaty</a> of 1819. The treaty took effect on February 22, 1821. Having settled its border with Spain, the U.S. admitted the southeastern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Missouri_Territory" title="Missouri Territory">Territory of Missouri</a> to the Union as the <a href="/wiki/Missouri" title="Missouri">state of Missouri</a> on August 10, 1821. The remainder of Missouri Territory, including what would become northeastern Colorado, became an unorganized territory and remained so for 33 years over the <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_the_United_States" title="Slavery in the United States">question of slavery</a>. After 11 years of war, Spain finally recognized the independence of Mexico with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Treaty of Córdoba">Treaty of Córdoba</a> signed on August 24, 1821. Mexico eventually ratified the Adams–Onís Treaty in 1831. The <a href="/wiki/Texian_Revolt" class="mw-redirect" title="Texian Revolt">Texian Revolt</a> of 1835–36 fomented a dispute between the U.S. and Mexico which eventually erupted into the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> in 1846. Mexico surrendered its northern territory to the U.S. with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Guadalupe_Hidalgo" title="Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo">Treaty of Guadalupe Hidalgo</a> after the war in 1848; this included much of the western and southern areas of Colorado.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG/220px-Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="194" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG/330px-Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG/440px-Mexican_Cession_in_Mexican_View.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1068" data-file-height="941" /></a><figcaption>Map of the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">Mexican Cession</a>, with the white representing the territory the United States received from Mexico (plus land ceded to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Texas" title="Republic of Texas">Republic of Texas</a>) after the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a>. Well over half of Colorado was received from this treaty.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Most American settlers first traveled to Colorado through the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_Trail" title="Santa Fe Trail">Santa Fe Trail</a>, which connected the U.S. to <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_New_Mexico" title="Santa Fe, New Mexico">Santa Fe</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Camino_Real_de_Tierra_Adentro" title="Camino Real de Tierra Adentro">Camino Real de Tierra Adentro</a> southward. Others were traveling overland west to the <a href="/wiki/Oregon_Country" title="Oregon Country">Oregon Country</a>, the new <a href="/wiki/California_gold_rush" title="California gold rush">goldfields of California</a>, or the new <a href="/wiki/Mormon" class="mw-redirect" title="Mormon">Mormon</a> settlements of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">State of Deseret</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_Valley" title="Salt Lake Valley">Salt Lake Valley</a>, avoided the rugged <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a>, and instead followed the <a href="/wiki/North_Platte_River" title="North Platte River">North Platte River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sweetwater_River_(Wyoming)" title="Sweetwater River (Wyoming)">Sweetwater River</a> to <a href="/wiki/South_Pass_(Wyoming)" title="South Pass (Wyoming)">South Pass (Wyoming)</a>, the lowest crossing of the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Divide">Continental Divide</a> between the Southern Rocky Mountains and the Central Rocky Mountains. In 1849, the Mormons of the Salt Lake Valley organized the extralegal <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">State of Deseret</a>, claiming the entire <a href="/wiki/Great_Basin" title="Great Basin">Great Basin</a> and all lands drained by the rivers <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Grand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado</a>. The federal government of the U.S. flatly refused to recognize the new Mormon government because it was <a href="/wiki/History_of_The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints#Brigham_Young&#39;s_early_theocratic_leadership" class="mw-redirect" title="History of The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">theocratic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_(law)" title="Sanctions (law)">sanctioned</a> <a href="/wiki/Mormonism_and_polygamy" title="Mormonism and polygamy">plural marriage</a>. Instead, the <a href="/wiki/Compromise_of_1850" title="Compromise of 1850">Compromise of 1850</a> divided the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Cession" title="Mexican Cession">Mexican Cession</a> and the northwestern claims of Texas into a new state and two new territories, the <a href="/wiki/State_of_California" class="mw-redirect" title="State of California">state of California</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_New_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of New Mexico">Territory of New Mexico</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Utah" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Utah">Territory of Utah</a>. On April 9, 1851, <a href="/wiki/Hispanos_of_New_Mexico" title="Hispanos of New Mexico">Hispano</a> settlers from the area of <a href="/wiki/Taos,_New_Mexico" title="Taos, New Mexico">Taos</a> settled the village of <a href="/wiki/San_Luis,_Colorado" title="San Luis, Colorado">San Luis</a>, then in the <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory" title="New Mexico Territory">New Mexico Territory</a>, as Colorado's first permanent <a href="/wiki/European_American" class="mw-redirect" title="European American">Euro-American</a> <a href="/wiki/Settlement_(migration)" class="mw-redirect" title="Settlement (migration)">settlement</a>, further cementing the traditions of <a href="/wiki/New_Mexican_cuisine" title="New Mexican cuisine">New Mexican cuisine</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_music" title="New Mexico music">New Mexico music</a> in the developing <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountain_Front" title="Southern Rocky Mountain Front">Southern Rocky Mountain Front</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lyons_2018_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lyons_2018-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sexton_2019_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sexton_2019-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1854, Senator <a href="/wiki/Stephen_A._Douglas" title="Stephen A. Douglas">Stephen A. Douglas</a> persuaded the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Congress">U.S. Congress</a> to divide the unorganized territory east of the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide" class="mw-redirect" title="Continental Divide">Continental Divide</a> into two new organized territories, the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Kansas" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Kansas">Territory of Kansas</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Nebraska" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Nebraska">Territory of Nebraska</a>, and an unorganized southern region known as the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Territory" title="Indian Territory">Indian Territory</a>. Each new territory was to decide the fate of slavery within its boundaries, but this compromise merely served to fuel animosity between <a href="/wiki/Free_soil" class="mw-redirect" title="Free soil">free soil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Proslavery_in_the_antebellum_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Proslavery in the antebellum United States">pro-slavery</a> factions.
</p><p>The gold seekers organized the <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Territory" title="Jefferson Territory">Provisional Government of the Territory of Jefferson</a> on August 24, 1859, but this new territory failed to secure approval from the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Congress of the United States">Congress of the United States</a> embroiled in the debate over slavery. The election of <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> for the President of the United States on November 6, 1860, led to the <a href="/wiki/Secession" title="Secession">secession</a> of nine southern <a href="/wiki/Slave_states" class="mw-redirect" title="Slave states">slave states</a> and the threat of <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">civil war among the states</a>. Seeking to augment the political power of the <a href="/wiki/Free_state_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Free state (United States)">Union states</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>-dominated Congress quickly admitted the eastern portion of the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Kansas" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Kansas">Territory of Kansas</a> into the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">Union</a> as the free <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">State of Kansas</a> on January 29, 1861, leaving the western portion of the Kansas Territory, and its gold-mining areas, as unorganized territory.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Territory_act">Territory act</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Territory act"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Organic_act#List_of_organic_acts" title="Organic act">Organic act §&#160;List of organic acts</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory" title="New Mexico Territory">New Mexico Territory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah_Territory" title="Utah Territory">Utah Territory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas%E2%80%93Nebraska_Act" title="Kansas–Nebraska Act">Kansas–Nebraska Act</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas Territory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Territory" title="Nebraska Territory">Nebraska Territory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Territory" title="Colorado Territory">Colorado Territory</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pike%27s_Peak_Gold_Rush" class="mw-redirect" title="Pike&#39;s Peak Gold Rush">Pike's Peak Gold Rush</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg/220px-1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg/330px-1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg/440px-1860_Colorado_Territory_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="448" data-file-height="303" /></a><figcaption>The territories of <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Territory" title="New Mexico Territory">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah_Territory" title="Utah Territory">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Territory" title="Kansas Territory">Kansas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nebraska_Territory" title="Nebraska Territory">Nebraska</a> before the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Thirty days later on February 28, 1861, outgoing U.S. President <a href="/wiki/James_Buchanan" title="James Buchanan">James Buchanan</a> signed an Act of Congress organizing the <a href="/wiki/Free_state_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Free state (United States)">free</a> <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ColoradoOrganicAct_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoOrganicAct-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> The original boundaries of Colorado remain unchanged except for government survey amendments. In 1776, Spanish priest <a href="/wiki/Silvestre_V%C3%A9lez_de_Escalante" class="mw-redirect" title="Silvestre Vélez de Escalante">Silvestre Vélez de Escalante</a> recorded that Native Americans in the area knew the river as <i><a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rio_Colorado" class="extiw" title="es:Rio Colorado">el Rio Colorado</a></i> for the red-brown silt that the river carried from the mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="The material near this tag failed verification of its source citation(s). (April 2021)">failed verification</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1859, a U.S. Army <a href="/wiki/Topography" title="Topography">topographic</a> expedition led by Captain <a href="/wiki/John_Navarre_Macomb,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="John Navarre Macomb, Jr.">John Macomb</a> located the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Grand_River_(Colorado)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand River (Colorado)">Grand River</a> in what is now <a href="/wiki/Canyonlands_National_Park" title="Canyonlands National Park">Canyonlands National Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Macomb_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macomb-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The Macomb party designated the confluence as the source of the Colorado River.
</p><p>On April 12, 1861, <a href="/wiki/South_Carolina" title="South Carolina">South Carolina</a> artillery opened fire on <a href="/wiki/Fort_Sumter" title="Fort Sumter">Fort Sumter</a> to start the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. While many gold seekers held sympathies for the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a>, the vast majority remained fiercely loyal to the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a> cause.
</p><p>In 1862, a force of Texas cavalry invaded the <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_New_Mexico" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of New Mexico">Territory of New Mexico</a> and captured <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_New_Mexico" title="Santa Fe, New Mexico">Santa Fe</a> on March 10. The object of this <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="New Mexico Campaign">Western Campaign</a> was to seize or disrupt Colorado and California's gold fields and seize Pacific Ocean ports for the Confederacy. A hastily organized force of Colorado volunteers force-marched from <a href="/wiki/Denver_City,_Colorado_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver City, Colorado Territory">Denver City, Colorado Territory</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Glorieta_Pass" title="Glorieta Pass">Glorieta Pass</a>, New Mexico Territory, in an attempt to block the Texans. On March 28, the Coloradans and local New Mexico volunteers stopped the Texans at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Glorieta_Pass" title="Battle of Glorieta Pass">Battle of Glorieta Pass</a>, destroyed their cannon and supply wagons, and dispersed 500 of their horses and mules.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The Texans were forced to retreat to Santa Fe. Having lost the supplies for their campaign and finding little support in New Mexico, the Texans abandoned Santa Fe and returned to <a href="/wiki/San_Antonio" title="San Antonio">San Antonio</a> in defeat. The Confederacy made no further attempts to seize the Southwestern United States.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg/220px-Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross.jpeg 1.5x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="191" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Mount_of_the_Holy_Cross" title="Mount of the Holy Cross">Mount of the Holy Cross</a>, photographed by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Jackson" title="William Henry Jackson">William Henry Jackson</a> in 1874</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 1864, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Colorado" title="Governor of Colorado">Territorial Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Evans_(Colorado_governor)" title="John Evans (Colorado governor)">John Evans</a> appointed the Reverend <a href="/wiki/John_Chivington" title="John Chivington">John Chivington</a> as Colonel of the Colorado Volunteers with orders to protect white settlers from <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne" title="Cheyenne">Cheyenne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arapaho" title="Arapaho">Arapaho</a> warriors who were accused of stealing cattle. Colonel Chivington ordered his troops to attack a band of Cheyenne and Arapaho encamped along Sand Creek. Chivington reported that his troops killed more than 500 warriors. The militia returned to Denver City in triumph, but several officers reported that the so-called battle was a blatant massacre of Indians at peace, that most of the dead were women and children, and that the bodies of the dead had been hideously mutilated and desecrated. Three U.S. Army inquiries condemned the action, and incoming President <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Johnson" title="Andrew Johnson">Andrew Johnson</a> asked Governor Evans for his resignation, but none of the perpetrators was ever punished. This event is now known as the <a href="/wiki/Sand_Creek_massacre" title="Sand Creek massacre">Sand Creek massacre</a>.
</p><p>In the midst and aftermath of the Civil War, many discouraged prospectors returned to their homes, but a few stayed and developed mines, mills, farms, ranches, roads, and towns in Colorado Territory. On September 14, 1864, James Huff discovered silver near <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Pass" title="Argentine Pass">Argentine Pass</a>, the first of many silver strikes. In 1867, the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a> laid its tracks west to Weir, now <a href="/wiki/Julesburg,_Colorado" title="Julesburg, Colorado">Julesburg</a>, in the northeast corner of the Territory. The Union Pacific linked up with the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Railroad" title="Central Pacific Railroad">Central Pacific Railroad</a> at <a href="/wiki/Promontory_Summit,_Utah" class="mw-redirect" title="Promontory Summit, Utah">Promontory Summit, Utah</a>, on May 10, 1869, to form the <a href="/wiki/First_transcontinental_railroad" title="First transcontinental railroad">First transcontinental railroad</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Denver_Pacific_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver Pacific Railway">Denver Pacific Railway</a> reached Denver in June of the following year, and the <a href="/wiki/Kansas_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Kansas Pacific">Kansas Pacific</a> arrived two months later to forge the second line across the continent. In 1872, rich veins of silver were discovered in the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Ute_tribe" class="mw-redirect" title="Ute tribe">Ute Indian</a> reservation in southwestern Colorado. The Ute people were removed from the San Juan Mountains the following year.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Statehood">Statehood</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Statehood"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Admission_to_the_Union" title="Admission to the Union">Admission to the Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_date_of_admission_to_the_Union" title="List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union">List of U.S. states by date of admission to the Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Silver_Boom" title="Colorado Silver Boom">Colorado Silver Boom</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cripple_Creek_Gold_Rush" title="Cripple Creek Gold Rush">Cripple Creek Gold Rush</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg/220px-Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="178" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg/330px-Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg/440px-Georgetown_loop_1899.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1192" data-file-height="967" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Loop" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgetown Loop">Georgetown Loop</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Central_Railroad" title="Colorado Central Railroad">Colorado Central Railroad</a> as photographed by <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Jackson" title="William Henry Jackson">William Henry Jackson</a> in 1899</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Forty-third_United_States_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Forty-third United States Congress">United States Congress</a> passed an enabling act on March 3, 1875, specifying the requirements for the Territory of Colorado to become a state.<sup id="cite_ref-ColoradoEnablingAct_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoEnablingAct-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> On August 1, 1876 (four weeks after the <a href="/wiki/Centennial_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Centennial of the United States">Centennial of the United States</a>), U.S. President Ulysses S. Grant signed a proclamation admitting Colorado to the Union as the 38th state and earning it the moniker "Centennial State".<sup id="cite_ref-ColoradoStatehoodProclamation_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoStatehoodProclamation-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The discovery of a major silver lode near <a href="/wiki/Leadville,_Colorado" title="Leadville, Colorado">Leadville</a> in 1878 triggered the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Silver_Boom" title="Colorado Silver Boom">Colorado Silver Boom</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Silver_Purchase_Act" title="Sherman Silver Purchase Act">Sherman Silver Purchase Act</a> of 1890 invigorated silver mining, and Colorado's last, but greatest, gold strike at <a href="/wiki/Cripple_Creek,_Colorado" title="Cripple Creek, Colorado">Cripple Creek</a> a few months later lured a new generation of gold seekers. Colorado women were granted the right to vote on November 7, 1893, making Colorado the second state to grant <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage</a> and the first one by a <a href="/wiki/1893_Colorado_women%27s_suffrage_referendum" title="1893 Colorado women&#39;s suffrage referendum">popular vote</a> (of Colorado men). The repeal of the Sherman Silver Purchase Act in 1893 led to a staggering collapse of the mining and agricultural economy of Colorado, but the state slowly and steadily recovered. Between the 1880s and 1930s, Denver's floriculture industry developed into a major industry in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> This period became known locally as the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Gold_Rush" title="Carnation Gold Rush">Carnation Gold Rush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Twentieth_and_twenty-first_centuries">Twentieth and twenty-first centuries</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Twentieth and twenty-first centuries"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg/170px-16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="229" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg/255px-16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg/340px-16th_street_denver_L.C_McClure.jpg 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="466" /></a><figcaption>16th Street in Denver in 1912</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg/220px-Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg/330px-Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg/440px-Ruins_of_Ludlow_restored.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5268" data-file-height="3248" /></a><figcaption>The ruins of the <a href="/wiki/Ludlow_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Ludlow massacre">Ludlow Colony</a> in the aftermath of the 1914 massacre.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Poor labor conditions and discontent among miners resulted in several major clashes between strikers and the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Army_National_Guard" title="Colorado Army National Guard">Colorado National Guard</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Labor_Wars" title="Colorado Labor Wars">1903–1904 Western Federation of Miners Strike</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Coalfield_War" title="Colorado Coalfield War">Colorado Coalfield War</a>, the latter of which included the <a href="/wiki/Ludlow_massacre" class="mw-redirect" title="Ludlow massacre">Ludlow massacre</a> that killed a dozen women and children.<sup id="cite_ref-Philip_Ross_1969_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Philip_Ross_1969-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Both the 1913–1914 Coalfield War and the <a href="/wiki/Denver_streetcar_strike_of_1920" title="Denver streetcar strike of 1920">Denver streetcar strike of 1920</a> resulted in federal troops intervening to end the violence.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In 1927, the <a href="/wiki/1927%E2%80%931928_Colorado_Coal_Strike" title="1927–1928 Colorado Coal Strike">1927-28 Colorado coal strike</a> occurred and was ultimately successful in winning a dollar a day increase in wages.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> During it however the <a href="/wiki/Columbine_Mine_massacre" title="Columbine Mine massacre">Columbine Mine massacre</a> resulted in six dead strikers following a confrontation with <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rangers" title="Colorado Rangers">Colorado Rangers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In a separate incident in <a href="/wiki/Trinidad,_Colorado" title="Trinidad, Colorado">Trinidad</a> the mayor was accused of deputizing members of the KKK against the striking workers.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> More than 5,000 Colorado miners—many immigrants—are estimated to have died in accidents since records were first formally collected following an 1884 accident in <a href="/wiki/Crested_Butte,_Colorado" title="Crested Butte, Colorado">Crested Butte</a> that killed 59.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1924, the <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Ku Klux Klan</a> Colorado Realm achieved dominance in Colorado politics. With peak membership levels, the <a href="/wiki/Ku_Klux_Klan#Second_Klan" title="Ku Klux Klan">Second Klan</a> levied significant control over both the local and state <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican parties</a>, particularly in the governor's office and city governments of Denver, <a href="/wiki/Canon_City,_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Canon City, Colorado">Cañon City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Durango,_Colorado" title="Durango, Colorado">Durango</a>. A particularly strong element of the Klan controlled the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Police_Department" title="Denver Police Department">Denver Police</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KKK_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KKK-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cross_burning" title="Cross burning">Cross burnings</a> became semi-regular occurrences in cities such as <a href="/wiki/Florence,_Colorado" title="Florence, Colorado">Florence</a> and Pueblo. The Klan targeted African-Americans, <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a>, Eastern European immigrants, and other non-White <a href="/wiki/Protestant" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> groups.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Efforts by non-Klan lawmen and lawyers including <a href="/wiki/Philip_S._Van_Cise" title="Philip S. Van Cise">Philip Van Cise</a> led to a rapid decline in the organization's power, with membership waning significantly by the end of the 1920s.<sup id="cite_ref-KKK_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KKK-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale,_1944.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale%2C_1944.png/220px-Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale%2C_1944.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale%2C_1944.png/330px-Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale%2C_1944.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale%2C_1944.png/440px-Three_10th_Mountain_Division_Skitroopers_above_Camp_Hale%2C_1944.png 2x" data-file-width="2366" data-file-height="1622" /></a><figcaption>Three <a href="/wiki/10th_Mountain_Division" title="10th Mountain Division">10th Mountain Division</a> skitroopers above <a href="/wiki/Camp_Hale" title="Camp Hale">Camp Hale</a> in February 1944</figcaption></figure>
<p>Colorado became the first western state to host a major political convention when the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> met in Denver in 1908. By the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census,_1930" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Census, 1930">U.S. census in 1930</a>, the population of Colorado first exceeded one million residents. Colorado suffered greatly through the <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dust_Bowl" title="Dust Bowl">Dust Bowl</a> of the 1930s, but a major wave of immigration following <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> boosted Colorado's fortune. Tourism became a mainstay of the state economy, and high technology became an important economic engine. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimated that the population of Colorado exceeded five million in 2009.
</p><p>On September 11, 1957, a plutonium fire occurred at the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Flats_Plant" title="Rocky Flats Plant">Rocky Flats Plant</a>, which resulted in the significant <a href="/wiki/Radioactive_contamination_from_the_Rocky_Flats_Plant" title="Radioactive contamination from the Rocky Flats Plant">plutonium contamination</a> of surrounding populated areas.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain,_Colorado_in_1961.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain%2C_Colorado_in_1961.jpg/220px-Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain%2C_Colorado_in_1961.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain%2C_Colorado_in_1961.jpg/330px-Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain%2C_Colorado_in_1961.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain%2C_Colorado_in_1961.jpg/440px-Skiers_on_Aspen_Mountain%2C_Colorado_in_1961.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2277" data-file-height="1683" /></a><figcaption>Skiers on <a href="/wiki/Aspen_Mountain_(ski_area)" title="Aspen Mountain (ski area)">Aspen Mountain</a> in 1961</figcaption></figure>
<p>From the 1940s and 1970s, many protest movements gained momentum in Colorado, predominantly in Denver. This included the <a href="/wiki/Chicano_Movement" title="Chicano Movement">Chicano Movement</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Civil_rights_movements" title="Civil rights movements">civil rights</a>, and social movement of <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Americans" title="Mexican Americans">Mexican Americans</a> emphasizing a <a href="/wiki/Chicano" title="Chicano">Chicano</a> identity that is widely considered to have begun in Denver.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The National <a href="/wiki/Chicano_Youth_Liberation_Conference" title="Chicano Youth Liberation Conference">Chicano Youth Liberation Conference</a> was held in Colorado in March 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1967, Colorado was the first state to loosen restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Colorado" title="Abortion in Colorado">abortion</a> when governor <a href="/wiki/John_Arthur_Love" title="John Arthur Love">John Love</a> signed a law allowing abortions in cases of rape, incest, or threats to the woman's mental or physical health. Many states followed Colorado's lead in loosening abortion laws in the 1960s and 1970s.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the late 1990s, Colorado has been the site of <a href="/wiki/List_of_shootings_in_Colorado" title="List of shootings in Colorado">multiple major</a> <a href="/wiki/Mass_shooting" title="Mass shooting">mass shootings</a>, including the infamous <a href="/wiki/Columbine_High_School_massacre" title="Columbine High School massacre">Columbine High School massacre</a> in 1999 which made international news, where <a href="/wiki/Eric_Harris_and_Dylan_Klebold" title="Eric Harris and Dylan Klebold">two gunmen</a> killed 12 students and one teacher, before committing suicide. The incident has spawned many <a href="/wiki/Columbine_effect" title="Columbine effect">copycat incidents</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> On July 20, 2012, a <a href="/wiki/2012_Aurora,_Colorado_shooting" class="mw-redirect" title="2012 Aurora, Colorado shooting">gunman killed 12 people</a> in a movie theater in <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Colorado" title="Aurora, Colorado">Aurora</a>. The state responded with tighter restrictions on firearms, including <a href="/wiki/High-capacity_magazine_ban" title="High-capacity magazine ban">introducing a limit</a> on <a href="/wiki/Magazine_(firearms)" title="Magazine (firearms)">magazine</a> capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> On March 22, 2021, a <a href="/wiki/2021_Boulder_shooting" title="2021 Boulder shooting">gunman killed 10 people</a>, including a police officer, in a <a href="/wiki/King_Soopers" title="King Soopers">King Soopers</a> supermarket in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In an instance of <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_LGBT_people" title="Violence against LGBT people">anti-LGBT violence</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs_nightclub_shooting" title="Colorado Springs nightclub shooting">gunman killed 5 people</a> at a nightclub in <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">Colorado Springs</a> during the night of November 19–20, 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Four warships of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Navy">U.S. Navy</a> have been named the <a href="/wiki/USS_Colorado" title="USS Colorado">USS <i>Colorado</i></a>. The first USS <i>Colorado</i> was named for the Colorado River and served in the Civil War and later the <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_Squadron" title="Asiatic Squadron">Asiatic Squadron</a>, where it was attacked during the 1871 <a href="/wiki/United_States_expedition_to_Korea" title="United States expedition to Korea">Korean Expedition</a>. The later three ships were named in honor of the state, including <a href="/wiki/USS_Colorado_(ACR-7)" title="USS Colorado (ACR-7)">an armored cruiser</a> and the <a href="/wiki/USS_Colorado_(BB-45)" title="USS Colorado (BB-45)">battleship USS <i>Colorado</i></a>, the latter of which was the lead ship of <a href="/wiki/Colorado-class_battleship" title="Colorado-class battleship">her class</a> and served in <a href="/wiki/War_in_the_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="War in the Pacific">World War II in the Pacific</a> beginning in 1941. At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a>, the battleship USS <i>Colorado</i> was located at the naval base in San Diego, California, and thus went unscathed. The most recent vessel to bear the name USS <i>Colorado</i> is <a href="/wiki/Virginia-class_submarine" title="Virginia-class submarine">Virginia-class submarine</a> <a href="/wiki/USS_Colorado_(SSN-788)" title="USS Colorado (SSN-788)">USS <i>Colorado</i> (SSN-788)</a>, which was commissioned in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Colorado" title="Geography of Colorado">Geography of Colorado</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg/220px-Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg/330px-Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg/440px-Colorado_geographic_map-en.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2581" data-file-height="2200" /></a><figcaption></figcaption></figure>
<p>Colorado is notable for its diverse geography, which includes alpine mountains, high plains, deserts with huge sand dunes, and deep canyons. In 1861, the <a href="/wiki/Thirty-sixth_United_States_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Thirty-sixth United States Congress">United States Congress</a> defined the boundaries of the new <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Territory of Colorado">Territory of Colorado</a> exclusively by lines of <a href="/wiki/Latitude" title="Latitude">latitude</a> and <a href="/wiki/Longitude" title="Longitude">longitude</a>, stretching from <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°N</a> to <a href="/wiki/41st_parallel_north" title="41st parallel north">41°N</a> latitude, and from <a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="25th meridian west from Washington">102°02′48″W</a> to <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">109°02′48″W</a> longitude (<a href="/wiki/25th_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="25th meridian west from Washington">25°W</a> to <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">32°W</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Meridian" class="mw-redirect" title="Washington Meridian">Washington Meridian</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ColoradoOrganicAct_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ColoradoOrganicAct-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> After <span class="currentage"></span>163 years of government surveys, the borders of Colorado were officially defined by 697 <a href="/wiki/Boundary_marker" title="Boundary marker">boundary markers</a> and 697 <a href="/wiki/Border" title="Border">straight boundary lines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FM_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FM-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> Colorado, <a href="/wiki/Wyoming" title="Wyoming">Wyoming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> are the only states that have their borders defined solely by straight boundary lines with no natural features.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The southwest corner of Colorado is the <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a> at <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">36°59′56″N</a>, <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">109°2′43″W</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FourCorners_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FourCorners-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FourCornersMonument_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FourCornersMonument-52">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a>, located at the place where Colorado, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> meet, is the only place in the United States where four states meet.<sup id="cite_ref-BT_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BT-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Plains">Plains</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Plains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Picketwire_Canyon.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Picketwire_Canyon.jpg/220px-Picketwire_Canyon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Picketwire_Canyon.jpg/330px-Picketwire_Canyon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Picketwire_Canyon.jpg/440px-Picketwire_Canyon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a><figcaption>The arid high plains in Southeastern Colorado</figcaption></figure>
<p>Approximately half of Colorado is flat and rolling land. East of the Rocky Mountains is the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Eastern_Plains" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado Eastern Plains">Colorado Eastern Plains</a> of the <a href="/wiki/High_Plains_(United_States)" title="High Plains (United States)">High Plains</a>, the section of the Great Plains within Colorado at elevations ranging from roughly 3,350 to 7,500 feet (1,020 to 2,290&#160;m).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The Colorado plains are mostly prairies but also include <a href="/wiki/Deciduous_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Deciduous forests">deciduous forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Butte" title="Butte">buttes</a>, and canyons. Precipitation averages 15 to 25 inches (380 to 640&#160;mm) annually.<sup id="cite_ref-ccc_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Eastern Colorado is presently mainly farmland and rangeland, along with small farming villages and towns. <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Corn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wheat" title="Wheat">wheat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">hay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soybean" title="Soybean">soybeans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Oat" title="Oat">oats</a> are all typical crops. Most villages and towns in this region boast both a water tower and a <a href="/wiki/Grain_elevator" title="Grain elevator">grain elevator</a>. Irrigation water is available from both surface and subterranean sources. Surface water sources include the <a href="/wiki/South_Platte" class="mw-redirect" title="South Platte">South Platte</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arkansas_River" title="Arkansas River">Arkansas River</a>, and a few other streams. Subterranean water is generally accessed through <a href="/wiki/Artesian_well" title="Artesian well">artesian wells</a>. Heavy usage of these wells for irrigation purposes caused underground water reserves to decline in the region. Eastern Colorado also hosts a considerable amount and range of livestock, such as cattle ranches and hog farms.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Front_Range">Front Range</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Front Range"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Condiv.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Condiv.JPG/220px-Condiv.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Condiv.JPG/330px-Condiv.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Condiv.JPG/440px-Condiv.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="2746" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a> Peaks west of Denver</figcaption></figure>
<p>Roughly 70% of Colorado's population resides along the eastern edge of the Rocky Mountains in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a> between <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne,_Wyoming" title="Cheyenne, Wyoming">Cheyenne, Wyoming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_Colorado" title="Pueblo, Colorado">Pueblo, Colorado</a>. This region is partially protected from prevailing storms that blow in from the Pacific Ocean region by the high Rockies in the middle of Colorado. The "Front Range" includes Denver, <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins,_Colorado" title="Fort Collins, Colorado">Fort Collins</a>, Loveland, <a href="/wiki/Castle_Rock,_Colorado" title="Castle Rock, Colorado">Castle Rock</a>, Colorado Springs, Pueblo, Greeley, and other townships and municipalities in between. On the other side of the Rockies, the significant population centers in western Colorado (which is known as "The Western Slope") are the cities of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction,_Colorado" title="Grand Junction, Colorado">Grand Junction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Durango,_Colorado" title="Durango, Colorado">Durango</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Colorado" title="Montrose, Colorado">Montrose</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mountains">Mountains</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mountains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1235681985">.mw-parser-output .side-box{margin:4px 0;box-sizing:border-box;border:1px solid #aaa;font-size:88%;line-height:1.25em;background-color:var(--background-color-interactive-subtle,#f8f9fa);display:flow-root}.mw-parser-output .side-box-abovebelow,.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{padding:0.25em 0.9em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-image{padding:2px 0 2px 0.9em;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-imageright{padding:2px 0.9em 2px 0;text-align:center}@media(min-width:500px){.mw-parser-output .side-box-flex{display:flex;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .side-box-text{flex:1;min-width:0}}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .side-box{width:238px}.mw-parser-output .side-box-right{clear:right;float:right;margin-left:1em}.mw-parser-output .side-box-left{margin-right:1em}}</style><div class="side-box metadata side-box-right"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style>
<div class="side-box-flex">
