</div>
</div></div></div>
</div>  
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mountain_peaks_of_Colorado" title="List of mountain peaks of Colorado">List of mountain peaks of Colorado</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mt._Elbert.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mt._Elbert.jpg/220px-Mt._Elbert.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="161" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mt._Elbert.jpg/330px-Mt._Elbert.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Mt._Elbert.jpg/440px-Mt._Elbert.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1096" data-file-height="802" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbert" title="Mount Elbert">Mount Elbert</a> at 14,440 feet (4,401.2&#160;m) is the highest summit of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a> and Colorado.</figcaption></figure>
<p>To the west of the Great Plains of Colorado rises the eastern slope of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. Notable peaks of the Rocky Mountains include <a href="/wiki/Longs_Peak" title="Longs Peak">Longs Peak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Blue_Sky" title="Mount Blue Sky">Mount Blue Sky</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak" title="Pikes Peak">Pikes Peak</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Peaks" title="Spanish Peaks">Spanish Peaks</a> near <a href="/wiki/Walsenburg,_Colorado" title="Walsenburg, Colorado">Walsenburg</a>, in southern Colorado. This area drains to the east and the southeast, ultimately either via the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>.
</p><p>The Rocky Mountains within Colorado contain 53 true peaks with a total of 58 that are 14,000 feet (4,267&#160;m) or higher in elevation above sea level, known as <a href="/wiki/Colorado_fourteeners" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado fourteeners">fourteeners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> These mountains are largely covered with trees such as <a href="/wiki/Conifer" title="Conifer">conifers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aspen" title="Aspen">aspens</a> up to the <a href="/wiki/Tree_line" title="Tree line">tree line</a>, at an elevation of about 12,000 feet (3,658&#160;m) in southern Colorado to about 10,500 feet (3,200&#160;m) in northern Colorado. Above this tree line, only alpine vegetation grows. Only small parts of the Colorado Rockies are snow-covered year-round.
</p><p>Much of the alpine snow melts by mid-August except for a few snow-capped peaks and a few small glaciers. The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mineral_Belt" title="Colorado Mineral Belt">Colorado Mineral Belt</a>, stretching from the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a> in the southwest to <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_City,_Colorado" title="Central City, Colorado">Central City</a> on the front range, contains most of the historic gold- and silver-mining districts of Colorado. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbert" title="Mount Elbert">Mount Elbert</a> is the highest summit of the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">Rocky Mountains</a>. The 30 <a href="/wiki/Highest_mountain_peaks_of_the_Rocky_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Highest mountain peaks of the Rocky Mountains">highest major summits</a> of the Rocky Mountains of North America are all within the state.
</p><p>The summit of Mount Elbert at 14,440 feet (4,401.2&#160;m) elevation in <a href="/wiki/Lake_County,_Colorado" title="Lake County, Colorado">Lake County</a> is the highest point in Colorado and the Rocky Mountains of North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Mount_Elbert_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mount_Elbert-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Colorado is the only U.S. state that lies entirely above 1,000 meters elevation. The point where the <a href="/wiki/Arikaree_River" title="Arikaree River">Arikaree River</a> flows out of <a href="/wiki/Yuma_County,_Colorado" title="Yuma County, Colorado">Yuma County, Colorado</a>, and into <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_County,_Kansas" title="Cheyenne County, Kansas">Cheyenne County, Kansas</a>, is the lowest in Colorado at 3,317 feet (1,011&#160;m) elevation. This point, which is the highest low elevation point of any state,<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> is higher than the high elevation points of 18 states and the District of Columbia.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Continental_Divide">Continental Divide</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Continental Divide"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Grays_Peak,_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Grays_Peak%2C_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg/170px-Grays_Peak%2C_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Grays_Peak%2C_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg/255px-Grays_Peak%2C_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Grays_Peak%2C_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg/340px-Grays_Peak%2C_Colorado_-_2007-06-17.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="800" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Grays_Peak" title="Grays Peak">Grays Peak</a>, at 14,278 feet (4,352&#160;m), is the highest point on the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide_of_the_Americas" title="Continental Divide of the Americas">Continental Divide</a> in North America.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Continental_Divide_of_the_Americas" title="Continental Divide of the Americas">Continental Divide of the Americas</a> extends along the crest of the Rocky Mountains. The area of Colorado to the west of the Continental Divide is called the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Western_Slope" title="Colorado Western Slope">Western Slope of Colorado</a>. West of the Continental Divide, water flows to the southwest via the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River_(U.S.)" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado River (U.S.)">Colorado River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_California" title="Gulf of California">Gulf of California</a>.
</p><p>Within the interior of the Rocky Mountains are several large parks which are high broad basins. In the north, on the east side of the Continental Divide is the <a href="/wiki/North_Park_(Colorado_basin)" title="North Park (Colorado basin)">North Park of Colorado</a>. The North Park is drained by the <a href="/wiki/North_Platte_River" title="North Platte River">North Platte River</a>, which flows north into Wyoming and Nebraska. Just to the south of North Park, but on the western side of the Continental Divide, is the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Park_(Colorado_basin)" title="Middle Park (Colorado basin)">Middle Park of Colorado</a>, which is drained by the Colorado River. The <a href="/wiki/South_Park_(Park_County,_Colorado)" title="South Park (Park County, Colorado)">South Park of Colorado</a> is the region of the <a href="/wiki/Headwater" class="mw-redirect" title="Headwater">headwaters</a> of the South Platte River.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="South_Central_region">South Central region</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: South Central region"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:ChicoClosedBasin.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChicoClosedBasin.jpg/220px-ChicoClosedBasin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChicoClosedBasin.jpg/330px-ChicoClosedBasin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/ChicoClosedBasin.jpg/440px-ChicoClosedBasin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="832" data-file-height="555" /></a><figcaption>The high desert lands that make up the San Luis Valley in Southern Colorado</figcaption></figure>
<p>In south-central Colorado is the large <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Valley" title="San Luis Valley">San Luis Valley</a>, where the headwaters of the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> are located. The northern part of the valley is the <a href="/wiki/San_Luis_Closed_Basin" title="San Luis Closed Basin">San Luis Closed Basin</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Endorheic_basin" title="Endorheic basin">endorheic basin</a> that helped created the <a href="/wiki/Great_Sand_Dunes" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Sand Dunes">Great Sand Dunes</a>. The valley sits between the <a href="/wiki/Sangre_De_Cristo_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Sangre De Cristo Mountains">Sangre De Cristo Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Mountains" title="San Juan Mountains">San Juan Mountains</a>. The Rio Grande drains due south into New Mexico, Texas, and Mexico. Across the <a href="/wiki/Sangre_de_Cristo_Range" title="Sangre de Cristo Range">Sangre de Cristo Range</a> to the east of the San Luis Valley lies the <a href="/wiki/Wet_Mountain_Valley" title="Wet Mountain Valley">Wet Mountain Valley</a>. These basins, particularly the San Luis Valley, lie along the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande_Rift" class="mw-redirect" title="Rio Grande Rift">Rio Grande Rift</a>, a major <a href="/wiki/Geological_formation" title="Geological formation">geological formation</a> of the Rocky Mountains, and its branches.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Western_Slope">Western Slope</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Western Slope"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Maroon_Bells_(11553)a.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Maroon_Bells_%2811553%29a.jpg/220px-Maroon_Bells_%2811553%29a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Maroon_Bells_%2811553%29a.jpg/330px-Maroon_Bells_%2811553%29a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Maroon_Bells_%2811553%29a.jpg/440px-Maroon_Bells_%2811553%29a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4466" data-file-height="2580" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Maroon_Bells" title="Maroon Bells">Maroon Bells</a>, at 14,163&#160;ft (4,317&#160;m), is part of <a href="/wiki/White_River_National_Forest" title="White River National Forest">White River National Forest</a> and a tourist destination</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Colorado_National_Monument_(4939640266).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg/220px-Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg/330px-Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg/440px-Colorado_National_Monument_%284939640266%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a><figcaption>The Colorado National Monument near Grand Junction is made up of high desert canyons and sandstone rock formations.</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Western Slope of Colorado includes the western face of the Rocky Mountains and all of the area to the western border. This area includes several terrains and climates from alpine mountains to arid deserts. The Western Slope includes many ski resort towns in the Rocky Mountains and towns west to Utah. It is less populous than the Front Range but includes a large number of national parks and monuments.
</p><p>The northwestern corner of Colorado is a sparsely populated region, and it contains part of the noted <a href="/wiki/Dinosaur_National_Monument" title="Dinosaur National Monument">Dinosaur National Monument</a>, which not only is a <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontological</a> area, but is also a scenic area of rocky hills, canyons, arid desert, and streambeds. Here, the Green River briefly crosses over into Colorado.
</p><p>The Western Slope of Colorado is drained by the Colorado River and its tributaries (primarily the <a href="/wiki/Gunnison_River" title="Gunnison River">Gunnison River</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_River_(Colorado_River)" class="mw-redirect" title="Green River (Colorado River)">Green River</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_River_(Colorado_River)" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan River (Colorado River)">San Juan River</a>). The Colorado River flows through <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Canyon" title="Glenwood Canyon">Glenwood Canyon</a>, and then through an arid valley made up of desert from <a href="/wiki/Rifle,_Colorado" title="Rifle, Colorado">Rifle</a> to <a href="/wiki/Parachute,_Colorado" title="Parachute, Colorado">Parachute</a>, through the desert canyon of <a href="/wiki/De_Beque_Canyon" title="De Beque Canyon">De Beque Canyon</a>, and into the arid desert of <a href="/wiki/Grand_Valley_(Colorado-Utah)" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Valley (Colorado-Utah)">Grand Valley</a>, where the city of Grand Junction is located.
</p><p>Also prominent is the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Mesa" title="Grand Mesa">Grand Mesa</a>, which lies to the southeast of Grand Junction; the high San Juan Mountains, a rugged mountain range; and to the north and west of the San Juan Mountains, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Plateau" title="Colorado Plateau">Colorado Plateau</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction,_Colorado" title="Grand Junction, Colorado">Grand Junction, Colorado</a>, at the confluence of the Colorado and Gunnison Rivers, is the largest city on the Western Slope. Grand Junction and Durango are the only major centers of <a href="/wiki/Television_broadcasting" class="mw-redirect" title="Television broadcasting">television broadcasting</a> west of the Continental Divide in Colorado, though most mountain resort communities publish daily newspapers. Grand Junction is located at the juncture of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Colorado" title="Interstate 70 in Colorado">Interstate 70</a> and US 50, the only major highways in western Colorado. Grand Junction is also along the major railroad of the Western Slope, the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Union Pacific">Union Pacific</a>. This railroad also provides the tracks for <a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyr</a></i> passenger train, which crosses the Rocky Mountains between Denver and Grand Junction.
</p><p>The Western Slope includes multiple notable destinations in the Colorado Rocky Mountains, including <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Springs,_Colorado" title="Glenwood Springs, Colorado">Glenwood Springs</a>, with its resort hot springs, and the <a href="/wiki/Ski_resort" title="Ski resort">ski resorts</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aspen,_Colorado" title="Aspen, Colorado">Aspen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breckenridge,_Colorado" title="Breckenridge, Colorado">Breckenridge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vail,_Colorado" title="Vail, Colorado">Vail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crested_Butte,_Colorado" title="Crested Butte, Colorado">Crested Butte</a>, <a href="/wiki/Steamboat_Springs,_Colorado" title="Steamboat Springs, Colorado">Steamboat Springs</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telluride,_Colorado" title="Telluride, Colorado">Telluride</a>.
</p><p>Higher education in and near the Western Slope can be found at <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mesa_University" title="Colorado Mesa University">Colorado Mesa University</a> in Grand Junction, <a href="/wiki/Western_Colorado_University" title="Western Colorado University">Western Colorado University</a> in Gunnison, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lewis_College" title="Fort Lewis College">Fort Lewis College</a> in Durango, and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mountain_College" title="Colorado Mountain College">Colorado Mountain College</a> in Glenwood Springs and Steamboat Springs.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a> in the southwest corner of Colorado marks the common boundary of Colorado, <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>; the only such place in the United States.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities and towns in Colorado">List of cities and towns in Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Colorado" title="List of counties in Colorado">List of counties in Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_rivers_of_Colorado" title="List of rivers of Colorado">List of rivers of Colorado</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Climate">Climate</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png/220px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="232" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png/330px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png/440px-K%C3%B6ppen_Climate_Types_Colorado.png 2x" data-file-width="1726" data-file-height="1823" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate types</a> of Colorado, using 1991-2020 <a href="/wiki/Climatological_normal" title="Climatological normal">climate normals</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> of Colorado is more complex than states outside of the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain States">Mountain States</a> region. Unlike most other states, southern Colorado is not always warmer than northern Colorado. Most of Colorado is made up of mountains, foothills, high plains, and desert lands. Mountains and surrounding valleys greatly affect the local climate.  Northeast, east, and southeast Colorado are mostly the high plains, while Northern Colorado is a mix of high plains, foothills, and mountains. Northwest and west Colorado are predominantly mountainous, with some desert lands mixed in. Southwest and southern Colorado are a complex mixture of desert and mountain areas.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Eastern_Plains">Eastern Plains</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Eastern Plains"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The climate of the Eastern Plains is <a href="/wiki/Semi-arid_climate" title="Semi-arid climate">semi-arid</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a>: <a href="/wiki/Cold_semi-arid_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Cold semi-arid climate"><i>BSk</i></a>) with low humidity and moderate precipitation, usually from 15 to 25 inches (380 to 640 millimeters) annually, although many areas near the rivers are semi-humid climate. The area is known for its abundant sunshine and cool, clear nights, which give this area a great average <a href="/wiki/Diurnal_temperature_variation" class="mw-redirect" title="Diurnal temperature variation">diurnal temperature range</a>. The difference between the highs of the days and the lows of the nights can be considerable as warmth dissipates to space during clear nights, the heat radiation not being trapped by clouds. The Front Range urban corridor, where most of the population of Colorado resides, lies in a pronounced <a href="/wiki/Rain_shadow" title="Rain shadow">precipitation shadow</a> as a result of being on the <a href="/wiki/Leeward" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeward">lee</a> side of the Rocky Mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-usgsFRUC1978_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-usgsFRUC1978-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In summer, this area can have many days above 95&#160;°F (35&#160;°C) and often 100&#160;°F (38&#160;°C).<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_of_Colorado_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_of_Colorado-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> On the plains, the winter lows usually range from 25 to −10&#160;°F (−4 to −23&#160;°C). About 75% of the precipitation falls within the growing season, from April to September, but this area is very prone to droughts. Most of the precipitation comes from thunderstorms, which can be severe, and from major snowstorms that occur in the winter and early spring. Otherwise, winters tend to be mostly dry and cold.<sup id="cite_ref-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In much of the region, March is the snowiest month. April and May are normally the rainiest months, while April is the wettest month overall. The Front Range cities closer to the mountains tend to be warmer in the winter due to <a href="/wiki/Chinook_wind" title="Chinook wind">Chinook winds</a> which warms the area, sometimes bringing temperatures of 70&#160;°F (21&#160;°C) or higher in the winter.<sup id="cite_ref-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denver-Colorado-United-States-of-America-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The average July temperature is 55&#160;°F (13&#160;°C) in the morning and 90&#160;°F (32&#160;°C) in the afternoon. The average January temperature is 18&#160;°F (−8&#160;°C) in the morning and 48&#160;°F (9&#160;°C) in the afternoon, although variation between consecutive days can be 40&#160;°F (22&#160;°C).
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Front_Range_foothills">Front Range foothills</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Front Range foothills"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Just west of the plains and into the foothills, there is a wide variety of climate types. Locations merely a few miles apart can experience entirely different weather depending on the topography. Most valleys have a semi-arid climate, not unlike the eastern plains, which transitions to an <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine climate</a> at the highest elevations. Microclimates also exist in local areas that run nearly the entire spectrum of climates, including subtropical highland (<i>Cfb/Cwb</i>), humid subtropical (<i>Cfa</i>), humid continental (<i>Dfa/Dfb</i>), Mediterranean (<i>Csa/Csb</i>) and subarctic (<i>Dfc</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Extreme_weather">Extreme weather</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Extreme weather"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Extreme weather changes are common in Colorado, although a significant portion of the extreme weather occurs in the least populated areas of the state. Thunderstorms are common east of the Continental Divide in the spring and summer, yet are usually brief. Hail is a common sight in the mountains east of the Divide and across the eastern Plains, especially the northeast part of the state. Hail is the most commonly reported warm-season severe weather hazard, and occasionally causes human injuries, as well as significant property damage.<sup id="cite_ref-Childs_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Childs-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The eastern Plains are subject to some of the biggest hail storms in North America.<sup id="cite_ref-ccc_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Notable examples are the severe hailstorms that hit Denver on July 11, 1990,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> and May 8, 2017, the latter being the costliest ever in the state.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Eastern Plains are part of the extreme western portion of <a href="/wiki/Tornado_Alley" title="Tornado Alley">Tornado Alley</a>; some damaging tornadoes in the Eastern Plains include the 1990 <a href="/wiki/Limon,_Colorado" title="Limon, Colorado">Limon</a> <a href="/wiki/Fujita_scale" title="Fujita scale">F3</a> tornado and the <a href="/wiki/Tornado_outbreak_of_May_22%E2%80%9327,_2008#Windsor,_Colorado" title="Tornado outbreak of May 22–27, 2008">2008 Windsor EF3 tornado</a>, which devastated a small town.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> Portions of the eastern Plains see especially frequent tornadoes, both those spawned from <a href="/wiki/Mesocyclone" title="Mesocyclone">mesocyclones</a> in <a href="/wiki/Supercell" title="Supercell">supercell</a> thunderstorms and from less intense <a href="/wiki/Landspout" title="Landspout">landspouts</a>, such as within the <a href="/wiki/Denver_convergence_vorticity_zone" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver convergence vorticity zone">Denver convergence vorticity zone</a> (DCVZ).<sup id="cite_ref-Childs_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Childs-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Plains are also susceptible to occasional floods and particularly severe flash floods, which are caused both by thunderstorms and by the rapid melting of snow in the mountains during warm weather. Notable examples include the <a href="/w/index.php?title=1965_Denver_Flood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1965 Denver Flood (page does not exist)">1965 Denver Flood</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Big_Thompson_River" title="Big Thompson River">Big Thompson River</a> flooding of 1976 and the <a href="/wiki/2013_Colorado_floods" title="2013 Colorado floods">2013 Colorado floods</a>. Hot weather is common during summers in Denver. The city's record in 1901 for the number of consecutive days above 90&#160;°F (32&#160;°C) was broken during the summer of 2008. The new record of 24 consecutive days surpassed the previous record by almost a week.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Much of Colorado is very dry, with the state averaging only 17 inches (430 millimeters) of precipitation per year statewide. The state rarely experiences a time when some portion is not in some degree of drought.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The lack of precipitation contributes to the severity of wildfires in the state, such as the <a href="/wiki/Hayman_Fire" title="Hayman Fire">Hayman Fire</a> of 2002. Other notable fires include the <a href="/wiki/Fourmile_Canyon#Fourmile_Canyon_Fire" title="Fourmile Canyon">Fourmile Canyon Fire</a> of 2010, the <a href="/wiki/Waldo_Canyon_Fire" title="Waldo Canyon Fire">Waldo Canyon Fire</a> and <a href="/wiki/High_Park_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="High Park Fire">High Park Fire</a> of June 2012, and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest_Fire" title="Black Forest Fire">Black Forest Fire</a> of June 2013. Even these fires were exceeded in severity by the <a href="/wiki/Pine_Gulch_Fire" title="Pine Gulch Fire">Pine Gulch Fire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Peak_Fire" title="Cameron Peak Fire">Cameron Peak Fire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/East_Troublesome_Fire" title="East Troublesome Fire">East Troublesome Fire</a> in 2020, all being the three largest fires in Colorado history (see <a href="/wiki/2020_Colorado_wildfires" title="2020 Colorado wildfires">2020 Colorado wildfires</a>). And the Marshall Fire which started on December 30, 2021, while not the largest in state history, was the most destructive ever in terms of property loss (see <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Fire" title="Marshall Fire">Marshall Fire</a>).
</p><p>However, some of the mountainous regions of Colorado receive a huge amount of moisture from winter snowfalls. The spring melts of these snows often cause great waterflows in the <a href="/wiki/Yampa_River" title="Yampa River">Yampa River</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">Colorado River</a>, the Rio Grande, the Arkansas River, the North Platte River, and the South Platte River.
</p><p>Water flowing out of the Colorado Rocky Mountains is a very significant source of water for the farms, towns, and cities of the southwest states of New Mexico, Arizona, Utah, and Nevada, as well as the Midwest, such as Nebraska and Kansas, and the southern states of Oklahoma and Texas. A significant amount of water is also diverted for use in California; occasionally (formerly naturally and consistently), the flow of water reaches northern Mexico.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate_change">Climate change</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate change"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="excerpt-block"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066933788">.mw-parser-output .excerpt-hat .mw-editsection-like{font-style:normal}</style><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink excerpt-hat selfref">These paragraphs are an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Colorado" title="Climate change in Colorado">Climate change in Colorado</a>.<span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_in_Colorado&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div><div class="excerpt">
<p><a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Colorado" title="Climate change in Colorado">Climate change in Colorado</a> encompasses the effects of <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, attributed to man-made increases in atmospheric <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide" title="Carbon dioxide">carbon dioxide</a>, in the U.S. state of Colorado.
</p><p>In 2019 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Denver_Post" title="The Denver Post">The Denver Post</a></i> reported that "[i]ndividuals living in southeastern Colorado are more vulnerable to potential health effects from climate change than residents in other parts of the state".<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">United States Environmental Protection Agency</a> has more broadly reported:
</p>
"Colorado's climate is changing. Most of the state has warmed one or two degrees (F) in the last century. Throughout the <a href="/wiki/Western_United_States" title="Western United States">western United States</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heat_wave" title="Heat wave">heat waves</a> are becoming more common, <a href="/wiki/Snow" title="Snow">snow</a> is melting earlier in spring, and less water flows through the Colorado River.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> Rising temperatures<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> and recent droughts<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> in the region have killed many trees by drying out soils, increasing the risk of forest fires, or enabling outbreaks of forest insects. In the coming decades, the changing climate is likely to decrease water availability and agricultural yields in Colorado, and further increase the risk of <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">wildfires</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Colorado_EPA_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Colorado_EPA-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup></div></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Records">Records</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Records"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The highest official ambient air temperature ever recorded in Colorado was 115&#160;°F (46.1&#160;°C) on July 20, 2019, at <a href="/wiki/John_Martin_Reservoir" title="John Martin Reservoir">John Martin Dam</a>. The lowest official air temperature was −61&#160;°F (−51.7&#160;°C) on February 1, 1985, at <a href="/wiki/Maybell,_Colorado" title="Maybell, Colorado">Maybell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-StateMaxTemps_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateMaxTemps-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-StateMinTemps_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-StateMinTemps-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Earthquakes">Earthquakes</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Earthquakes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Despite its mountainous terrain, Colorado is relatively quiet seismically. The U.S. <a href="/wiki/National_Earthquake_Information_Center" title="National Earthquake Information Center">National Earthquake Information Center</a> is located in <a href="/wiki/Golden,_Colorado" title="Golden, Colorado">Golden</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>On August 22, 2011, a <a href="/wiki/2011_Colorado_earthquake" title="2011 Colorado earthquake">5.3 magnitude earthquake</a> occurred 9 miles (14&#160;km) west-southwest of the city of <a href="/wiki/Trinidad,_Colorado" title="Trinidad, Colorado">Trinidad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> There were no casualties and only a small amount of damage was reported. It was the second-largest earthquake in Colorado's history, the largest being a <a href="/wiki/1882_Fort_Collins_earthquake" title="1882 Fort Collins earthquake">magnitude 6.6 earthquake</a>, recorded in 1882.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Four minor earthquakes rattled Colorado on August 24, 2018, ranging from magnitude 2.9 to 4.3.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> As of June 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there were 525 recorded earthquakes in Colorado since 1973, a majority of which range 2&#160;to 3.5 on the Richter scale.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Fauna">Fauna</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Fauna"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information&#32;on the lists of: <a href="/wiki/List_of_amphibians_of_Colorado" title="List of amphibians of Colorado">amphibians</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Colorado" title="List of birds of Colorado">birds</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Colorado" title="List of mammals of Colorado">mammals</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_reptiles_of_Colorado" title="List of reptiles of Colorado">reptiles</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Colorado_Wolf_-_Colorado_Taxidermist,_Edwin_Carter,_Collection_in_Breckenridge,_Mounted_Wolf_from_a_kill_in_Colorado_Rockies.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="Photo of Breckenridge naturalist Edwin Carter standing next to a taxidermied gray wolf killed in the Colorado Rockies, circa. 1890–1900" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Colorado_Wolf_-_Colorado_Taxidermist%2C_Edwin_Carter%2C_Collection_in_Breckenridge%2C_Mounted_Wolf_from_a_kill_in_Colorado_Rockies.jpg/170px-Colorado_Wolf_-_Colorado_Taxidermist%2C_Edwin_Carter%2C_Collection_in_Breckenridge%2C_Mounted_Wolf_from_a_kill_in_Colorado_Rockies.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="231" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Colorado_Wolf_-_Colorado_Taxidermist%2C_Edwin_Carter%2C_Collection_in_Breckenridge%2C_Mounted_Wolf_from_a_kill_in_Colorado_Rockies.jpg/255px-Colorado_Wolf_-_Colorado_Taxidermist%2C_Edwin_Carter%2C_Collection_in_Breckenridge%2C_Mounted_Wolf_from_a_kill_in_Colorado_Rockies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/45/Colorado_Wolf_-_Colorado_Taxidermist%2C_Edwin_Carter%2C_Collection_in_Breckenridge%2C_Mounted_Wolf_from_a_kill_in_Colorado_Rockies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="295" data-file-height="400" /></a><figcaption>Breckenridge naturalist <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Carter" title="Edwin Carter">Edwin Carter</a> with a mounted <a href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Gray wolf">gray wolf</a> killed in the Colorado Rockies, ca. 1890–1900</figcaption></figure>
<p>A process of extirpation by trapping and poisoning of the <a href="/wiki/Gray_wolf" class="mw-redirect" title="Gray wolf">gray wolf</a> (<i>Canis lupus</i>) from Colorado in the 1930s saw the last wild wolf in the state shot in 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-SierraWolf_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SierraWolf-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Repopulation_of_wolves_in_Colorado" title="Repopulation of wolves in Colorado">wolf pack recolonized Moffat County, Colorado</a> in northwestern Colorado in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> Cattle farmers have expressed concern that a returning wolf population potentially threatens their herds.<sup id="cite_ref-SierraWolf_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SierraWolf-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Coloradans <a href="/wiki/2020_Colorado_Proposition_114" title="2020 Colorado Proposition 114">voted to reintroduce gray wolves</a> in 2020, with the state committing to a plan to have a population in the state by 2022 and permitting non-lethal methods of driving off wolves attacking livestock and pets.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While there is fossil evidence of <a href="/wiki/Harrington%27s_mountain_goat" title="Harrington&#39;s mountain goat">Harrington's mountain goat</a> in Colorado between at least 800,000 years ago and its extinction with <a href="/wiki/Megafauna" title="Megafauna">megafauna</a> roughly 11,000 years ago, the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_goat" title="Mountain goat">mountain goat</a> is not native to Colorado but was instead introduced to the state over time during the interval between 1947 and 1972. Despite being an artificially-introduced species, the state declared mountain goats a native species in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, 2014, and 2019, an unknown illness killed nearly all mountain goat kids, leading to a <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Parks_and_Wildlife" title="Colorado Parks and Wildlife">Colorado Parks and Wildlife</a> investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The native population of <a href="/wiki/Pronghorn" title="Pronghorn">pronghorn</a> in Colorado has varied wildly over the last century, reaching a low of only 15,000 individuals during the 1960s. However, conservation efforts succeeded in bringing the stable population back up to roughly 66,000 by 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The population was estimated to have reached 85,000 by 2019 and had increasingly more run-ins with the increased suburban housing along the eastern Front Range. State wildlife officials suggested that landowners would need to modify fencing to allow the greater number of pronghorns to move unabated through the newly developed land.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Pronghorns are most readily found in the northern and eastern portions of the state, with some populations also in the western San Juan Mountains.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Common wildlife found in the mountains of Colorado include <a href="/wiki/Mule_deer" title="Mule deer">mule deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_red_squirrel" title="Southwestern red squirrel">southwestern red squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Golden-mantled_ground_squirrel" title="Golden-mantled ground squirrel">golden-mantled ground squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yellow-bellied_marmot" title="Yellow-bellied marmot">yellow-bellied marmot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moose" title="Moose">moose</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_pika" title="American pika">American pika</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Red_fox" title="Red fox">red fox</a>, all at exceptionally high numbers, though moose are not native to the state.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> The foothills include <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">deer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fox_squirrel" title="Fox squirrel">fox squirrel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desert_cottontail" title="Desert cottontail">desert cottontail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountain_cottontail" title="Mountain cottontail">mountain cottontail</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Coyote" title="Coyote">coyote</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The prairies are home to <a href="/wiki/Black-tailed_prairie_dog" title="Black-tailed prairie dog">black-tailed prairie dog</a>, the endangered <a href="/wiki/Swift_fox" title="Swift fox">swift fox</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_badger" title="American badger">American badger</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_jackrabbit" title="White-tailed jackrabbit">white-tailed jackrabbit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Counties">Counties</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Counties"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1235681985"><div class="side-box metadata side-box-right"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">
<div class="side-box-flex">

<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" data-expandtext="show links" data-collapsetext="Hide">

</p>

</div>
</div></div></div>
</div>  
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_counties_in_Colorado" title="List of counties in Colorado">List of counties in Colorado</a></div>
<p>The State of Colorado is divided into 64 <a href="/wiki/County_(United_States)" title="County (United States)">counties</a>. Two of these counties, the <a href="/wiki/Broomfield,_Colorado" title="Broomfield, Colorado">City and County of Broomfield</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">City and County of Denver</a>, have <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidated city and county governments</a>. Counties are important units of government in Colorado since there are no <a href="/wiki/Civil_township" title="Civil township">civil townships</a> or other <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_division" title="Minor civil division">minor civil divisions</a>.
</p><p>The most populous county in Colorado is <a href="/wiki/El_Paso_County,_Colorado" title="El Paso County, Colorado">El Paso County</a>, the home of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">City of Colorado Springs</a>. The second most populous county is the <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">City and County of Denver</a>, the state capital. Five of the 64 counties now have more than 500,000 residents, while 12 have fewer than 5,000 residents. The ten most populous Colorado counties are all located in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mesa_County,_Colorado" title="Mesa County, Colorado">Mesa County</a> is the most populous county on the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Western_Slope" title="Colorado Western Slope">Colorado Western Slope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2023_county_estimates_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2023_county_estimates-103">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Municipalities">Municipalities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Municipalities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1235681985"><div class="side-box metadata side-box-right"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">
<div class="side-box-flex">

<div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" data-expandtext="show links" data-collapsetext="Hide">

</p>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">List of municipalities in Colorado</a></div>
<p>Colorado has 272 <a href="/wiki/Municipal_corporation" title="Municipal corporation">active incorporated municipalities</a>, comprising 197 <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">towns</a>, 73 <a href="/wiki/City" title="City">cities</a>, and two <a href="/wiki/Consolidated_city-county" title="Consolidated city-county">consolidated city and county governments</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MuniIncCO_104-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MuniIncCO-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Colorado_incplace_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_incplace-113">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_census" title="2020 United States census">2020 United States census</a>, 4,299,942 of the 5,773,714 Colorado residents (74.47%) lived in one of these 272 municipalities. Another 714,417 residents (12.37%) lived in one of the 210 <a href="/wiki/List_of_census-designated_places_in_Colorado" title="List of census-designated places in Colorado">census-designated places</a>, while the remaining 759,355 residents (13.15%) lived in the many rural and mountainous areas of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Colorado municipalities operate under one of five types of municipal governing authority. Colorado currently has <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Consolidated_city_and_county" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">two consolidated city and county governments</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Home_rule_municipality" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">61 home rule cities</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Statutory_city" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">12 statutory cities</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Home_rule_municipality" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">35 home rule towns</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Statutory_town" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">161 statutory towns</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Territorial_charter_municipality" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">one territorial charter municipality</a>.
</p><p>The most populous municipality is the <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">City and County of Denver</a>. Colorado has 12 municipalities with more than 100,000 residents, and 17 with fewer than 100 residents. The 16 most populous Colorado municipalities are all located in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction,_Colorado" title="Grand Junction, Colorado">City of Grand Junction</a> is the most populous municipality on the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Western_Slope" title="Colorado Western Slope">Colorado Western Slope</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Carbonate,_Colorado" title="Carbonate, Colorado">Town of Carbonate</a> has had no year-round population since the <a href="/wiki/1890_United_States_census" title="1890 United States census">1890 census</a> due to its severe winter weather and difficult access.<sup id="cite_ref-2023_muni_estimates_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2023_muni_estimates-115">&#91;l&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Unincorporated_communities">Unincorporated communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Unincorporated communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1235681985"><div class="side-box metadata side-box-right"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1126788409">
<div class="side-box-flex">
<div class="side-box-text plainlist"><b>Map this section's coordinates&#32;in "List of census-designated places in Colorado" using</b> <a class="external text" href="https://tools.wmflabs.org/osm4wiki/cgi-bin/wiki/wiki-osm.pl?project=en&amp;article=List+of+census-designated+places+in+Colorado&amp;section=Census-designated+places">OpenStreetMap</a>

</p>
<div class="mw-collapsible-content">

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_census-designated_places_in_Colorado" title="List of census-designated places in Colorado">List of census-designated places in Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_populated_places_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of populated places in Colorado">List of populated places in Colorado</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg/220px-HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg/330px-HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg/440px-HighlandsRanchAerial_CreditJohnChristensen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="2250" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Highlands_Ranch,_Colorado" title="Highlands Ranch, Colorado">Highlands Ranch, Colorado</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In addition to its 272 municipalities, Colorado has 210 <a href="/wiki/Unincorporated_area" title="Unincorporated area">unincorporated</a> <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated places (CDPs)</a> and many other small communities. The most populous unincorporated community in Colorado is <a href="/wiki/Highlands_Ranch,_Colorado" title="Highlands Ranch, Colorado">Highlands Ranch</a> south of Denver. The seven most populous CDPs are located in the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Clifton,_Colorado" title="Clifton, Colorado">Clifton CDP</a> is the most populous CDP on the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Western_Slope" title="Colorado Western Slope">Colorado Western Slope</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CO_CDP_2020_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CO_CDP_2020-116">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_districts">Special districts</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Special districts"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Colorado has more than 4,000 <a href="/wiki/Special_district_(United_States)" title="Special district (United States)">special districts</a>, most with <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">property tax</a> authority. These districts may provide schools, law enforcement, fire protection, water, sewage, drainage, irrigation, transportation, recreation, infrastructure, cultural facilities, business support, redevelopment, or other services.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train,_USTH.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train%2C_USTH.jpg/220px-RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train%2C_USTH.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train%2C_USTH.jpg/330px-RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train%2C_USTH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train%2C_USTH.jpg/440px-RTD_No._4018_A_Line_train%2C_USTH.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a><figcaption>A <a href="/wiki/Regional_Transportation_District" title="Regional Transportation District">Regional Transportation District</a> A Line train at <a href="/wiki/Denver_Union_Station" title="Denver Union Station">Denver Union Station</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p>Some of these districts have the authority to levy sales tax as well as property tax and use fees. This has led to a hodgepodge of sales tax and property tax rates in Colorado. There are some street intersections in Colorado with a different sales tax rate on each corner, sometimes substantially different.
</p><p>Some of the more notable Colorado districts are:
</p>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Regional_Transportation_District" title="Regional Transportation District">Regional Transportation District</a> (RTD), which affects the counties of Denver, Boulder, Jefferson, and portions of Adams, Arapahoe, Broomfield, and Douglas Counties</li></ul>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg/220px-Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg/330px-Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg/440px-Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science_View_from_north_west.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4107" data-file-height="2738" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science" title="Denver Museum of Nature and Science">Denver Museum of Nature and Science</a>, one the many organizations funded by the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_and_Cultural_Facilities_District" title="Scientific and Cultural Facilities District">Scientific and Cultural Facilities District</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Scientific_and_Cultural_Facilities_District" title="Scientific and Cultural Facilities District">Scientific and Cultural Facilities District</a> (SCFD), a special regional tax district with physical boundaries contiguous with county boundaries of Adams, Arapahoe, Boulder, Broomfield, Denver, Douglas, and Jefferson Counties
<ul><li>It is a 0.1% retail sales and uses tax (one penny on every $10).</li>
<li>According to the Colorado statute, the SCFD distributes the money to local organizations on an annual basis. These organizations must provide for the enlightenment and entertainment of the public through the production, presentation, exhibition, advancement, or preservation of art, music, theater, dance, zoology, botany, natural history, or cultural history.</li>
<li>As directed by statute, SCFD recipient organizations are currently divided into three "tiers" among which receipts are allocated by percentage.
<ul><li>Tier I includes regional organizations: the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Art_Museum" title="Denver Art Museum">Denver Art Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Botanic_Gardens" title="Denver Botanic Gardens">Denver Botanic Gardens</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Museum_of_Nature_and_Science" title="Denver Museum of Nature and Science">Denver Museum of Nature and Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Zoo" title="Denver Zoo">Denver Zoo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Center_for_the_Performing_Arts" title="Denver Center for the Performing Arts">Denver Center for the Performing Arts</a>. It receives 65.5%.</li>
<li>Tier II currently includes 26 regional organizations. Tier II receives 21%.</li>
<li>Tier III has more than 280 local organizations such as small theaters, orchestras, art centers, natural history, cultural history, and community groups. Tier III organizations apply for funding from the county cultural councils via a grant process. This tier receives 13.5%.</li></ul></li>
<li>An 11-member board of directors oversees the distributions by the Colorado Revised Statutes. Seven board members are appointed by county commissioners (in Denver, the Denver City Council) and four members are appointed by the Governor of Colorado.</li></ul></li>
<li>The Football Stadium District (FD or FTBL), approved by the voters to pay for and help build the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a>' stadium <a href="/wiki/Empower_Field_at_Mile_High" title="Empower Field at Mile High">Empower Field at Mile High</a>.</li>
<li>Local Improvement Districts (LID) within designated areas of Jefferson and Broomfield counties.</li>
<li>The Metropolitan Major League Baseball Stadium District, approved by voters to pay for and help build the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>' stadium <a href="/wiki/Coors_Field" title="Coors Field">Coors Field</a>.</li>
<li>Regional Transportation Authority (RTA) taxes at varying rates in Basalt, Carbondale, Glenwood Springs, and Gunnison County.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Statistical_areas">Statistical areas</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Statistical areas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_statistical_areas_in_Colorado" title="List of statistical areas in Colorado">List of statistical areas in Colorado</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png/220px-Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png/330px-Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png/440px-Colorado_CBSAs_2020.png 2x" data-file-width="5415" data-file-height="2656" /></a><figcaption>An enlargeable map of the 17 core-based statistical areas of Colorado</figcaption></figure>
<p>Most recently on March 6, 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Management_and_Budget" title="Office of Management and Budget">Office of Management and Budget</a> defined 21 statistical areas for Colorado comprising four <a href="/wiki/Combined_statistical_area" title="Combined statistical area">combined statistical areas</a>, seven <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan statistical areas</a>, and ten <a href="/wiki/Micropolitan_statistical_area" title="Micropolitan statistical area">micropolitan statistical areas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OMB-20-01_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMB-20-01-117">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most populous of the seven <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_statistical_area" title="Metropolitan statistical area">metropolitan statistical areas</a> in Colorado is the 10-county <a href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora-Lakewood,_CO_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver-Aurora-Lakewood, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora-Lakewood, CO Metropolitan Statistical Area</a> with a population of 2,963,821 at the <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 United States Census">2020 United States census</a>, an increase of +15.29% since the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2010 United States Census">2010 census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The more extensive 12-county <a href="/wiki/Denver-Aurora,_CO_Combined_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver-Aurora, CO Combined Statistical Area">Denver-Aurora, CO Combined Statistical Area</a> had a population of 3,623,560 at the 2020 census, an increase of +17.23% since the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The most populous extended metropolitan region in Rocky Mountain Region is the 18-county <a href="/wiki/Front_Range_Urban_Corridor" class="mw-redirect" title="Front Range Urban Corridor">Front Range Urban Corridor</a> along the northeast face of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Rocky_Mountains" title="Southern Rocky Mountains">Southern Rocky Mountains</a>. This region with Denver at its center had a population of 5,055,344 at the 2020 census, an increase of +16.65% since the 2010 census.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Colorado_population_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Colorado_population_map.png/350px-Colorado_population_map.png" decoding="async" width="350" height="200" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Colorado_population_map.png/525px-Colorado_population_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/56/Colorado_population_map.png 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="400" /></a><figcaption>Colorado population density map</figcaption></figure>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimated the population of Colorado on July 1, 2023, at 5,877,610, a 1.80% increase since the  <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_Census" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 United States Census">2020 United States census</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid #a2a9b1;background-color:var(--background-color-neutral-subtle,#f8f9fa);padding:0.3em;font-size:95%}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop caption{background-color:lavender;color:black;padding-right:0.2em;padding-left:0.2em;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold;border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-bottom:none}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop th[scope=col]{border-bottom:1px solid black}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td:nth-child(2){text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;padding-right:0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td.us-census-pop-estimate{padding-left:0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td:nth-child(3){padding-left:0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop td:nth-child(4){padding-left:0.5em;text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-footnote{border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:center}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-right{float:right;clear:right;margin:0 0 1em 1em}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-left{float:left;clear:left;margin:0 1em 1em 0}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-center{float:none;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop-none{float:none;margin:0 1em 1em 0}}</style>
</p>

font-weight: bold;"><div>Legend</div></div> <ul class="mw-collapsible-content" style="margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit; list-style: none; margin-left: 0;"><li style="line-height: inherit; margin: 0"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1216972533">.mw-parser-output .col-begin{border-collapse:collapse;padding:0;color:inherit;width:100%;border:0;margin:0}.mw-parser-output .col-begin-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .col-break{vertical-align:top;text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .col-break-2{width:50%}.mw-parser-output .col-break-3{width:33.3%}.mw-parser-output .col-break-4{width:25%}.mw-parser-output .col-break-5{width:20%}@media(max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .col-begin,.mw-parser-output .col-begin>tbody,.mw-parser-output .col-begin>tbody>tr,.mw-parser-output .col-begin>tbody>tr>td{display:block!important;width:100%!important}.mw-parser-output .col-break{padding-left:0!important}}</style><div> <table class="col-begin" role="presentation">  <tbody><tr> <td class="col-break col-break-2">  <b>Non-Hispanic White</b>  <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r981673959">.mw-parser-output .legend{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .legend-color{display:inline-block;min-width:1.25em;height:1.25em;line-height:1.25;margin:1px 0;text-align:center;border:1px solid black;background-color:transparent;color:black}.mw-parser-output .legend-text{}</style><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#dd7e6b; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;40–50%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#cc4125; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;50–60%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#a61c00; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;60–70%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#85200c; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;70–80%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#5b0f00; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;80–90%</div>   </td> <td class="col-break col-break-2">  <b>Hispanic or Latino</b>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#a2c4c9; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;40–50%</div>  <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#76a5af; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;50–60%</div>  &#32; </td></tr></tbody></table></div> </li></ul> </div></figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hispanics_and_Latinos_in_Colorado" title="Hispanics and Latinos in Colorado">Coloradan Hispanics and Latinos</a> (of any race and heritage) made up 20.7% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> According to the 2000 census, the largest ancestry groups in Colorado are <a href="/wiki/German_Americans" title="German Americans">German</a> (22%), <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Americans" title="Mexican Americans">Mexican</a> (18%), <a href="/wiki/Irish_Americans" title="Irish Americans">Irish</a> (12%), and <a href="/wiki/English_Americans" title="English Americans">English</a> (12%). Persons reporting German ancestry are especially numerous in the Front Range, the Rockies (west-central counties), and Eastern parts/High Plains.
</p><p>Colorado has a high proportion of <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a>, mostly <a href="/wiki/Mexican-American" class="mw-redirect" title="Mexican-American">Mexican-American</a>, citizens in Metropolitan Denver, Colorado Springs, as well as the smaller cities of Greeley and Pueblo, and elsewhere. Southern, Southwestern, and Southeastern Colorado have a large number of Hispanos, the descendants of the early settlers of colonial Spanish origin. In 1940, the U.S. Census Bureau reported Colorado's population as 8.2% Hispanic and 90.3% non-Hispanic White.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The Hispanic population of Colorado has continued to grow quickly over the past decades. By 2019, Hispanics made up 22% of Colorado's population, and <a href="/wiki/Non-Hispanic_White" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-Hispanic White">Non-Hispanic Whites</a> made up 70%.<sup id="cite_ref-quickfacts.census.gov_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-quickfacts.census.gov-127">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Spoken English in Colorado has many Spanish idioms.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Colorado also has some large African-American communities located in Denver, in the neighborhoods of Montbello, Five Points, Whittier, and many other East Denver areas. The state has sizable numbers of Asian-Americans of <a href="/wiki/Mongolian_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Mongolian American">Mongolian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chinese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Chinese American">Chinese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Filipino_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Filipino American">Filipino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korean_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Korean American">Korean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asian" class="mw-redirect" title="Southeast Asian">Southeast Asian</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japanese_American" class="mw-redirect" title="Japanese American">Japanese</a> descent. The highest population of Asian Americans can be found on the south and southeast side of Denver, as well as some on Denver's southwest side. The Denver metropolitan area is considered more liberal and diverse than much of the state when it comes to political issues and environmental concerns.
</p><p>The population of Native Americans in the state is small. Native Americans are concentrated in metropolitan Denver and the southwestern corner of Colorado, where there are two Ute reservations.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The majority of Colorado's immigrants are from <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There were a total of 70,331 births in Colorado in 2006. (Birth rate of 14.6 per thousand.) In 2007, non-Hispanic Whites were involved in 59.1% of all births.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Some 14.06% of those births involved a non-Hispanic White person and someone of a different race, most often with a couple including one Hispanic. A birth where at least one Hispanic person was involved counted for 43% of the births in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> As of the <a href="/wiki/2010_United_States_census" title="2010 United States census">2010 census</a>, Colorado has the seventh highest percentage of Hispanics (20.7%) in the U.S. behind <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a> (46.3%), California (37.6%), <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a> (37.6%), <a href="/wiki/Arizona" title="Arizona">Arizona</a> (29.6%), <a href="/wiki/Nevada" title="Nevada">Nevada</a> (26.5%), and Florida (22.5%). Per the 2000 census, the Hispanic population is estimated to be 918,899, or approximately 20% of the state's total population. Colorado has the 5th-largest population of Mexican-Americans, behind California, Texas, Arizona, and <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a>. In percentages, Colorado has the 6th-highest percentage of Mexican-Americans, behind New Mexico, California, Texas, Arizona, and Nevada.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Birth_data">Birth data</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Birth data"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In 2011, 46% of Colorado's population younger than the age of one were minorities, meaning that they had at least one parent who was not non-Hispanic White.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Note: Births in table do not add up, because Hispanics are counted both by their ethnicity and by their race, giving a higher overall number.</i>
</p>
