<p>In 2017, Colorado recorded the second-lowest fertility rate in the United States outside of New England, after <a href="/wiki/Oregon" title="Oregon">Oregon</a>, at 1.63 children per woman.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-140">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Significant contributing factors to the decline in pregnancies were the <a href="/wiki/Title_X" title="Title X"> Title X Family Planning Program</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Intrauterine_device" title="Intrauterine device">intrauterine device</a> grant from <a href="/wiki/Warren_Buffett" title="Warren Buffett">Warren Buffett</a>'s family.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Language">Language</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Language"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Native_American_languages_of_Colorado" title="Native American languages of Colorado">Native American languages of Colorado</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a>, the official language of the state, is the most commonly spoken language in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The second most commonly spoken language in the state is the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish language</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River_Numic_language" title="Colorado River Numic language">Colorado River Numic language</a>, also known as the <a href="/wiki/Ute_dialect" title="Ute dialect">Ute dialect</a>, is still spoken in Colorado.
</p>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Blue; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Protestantism_in_the_United_States" title="Protestantism in the United States">Protestantism</a> (39%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Purple; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Catholicism_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholicism in the United States">Catholicism</a> (19%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Teal; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Mormonism" title="Mormonism">Mormonism</a> (2%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Yellow; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</a> (1%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Green; color:white;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Unitarianism" title="Unitarianism">Unitarianism</a>/<a href="/wiki/Unitarian_Universalism" title="Unitarian Universalism">Universalism</a> (1%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:White; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Irreligion_in_the_United_States" title="Irreligion in the United States">Unaffiliated</a> (34%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Red; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a> (2%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Pink; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a> (1%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:Orange; color:black;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_United_States" title="Hinduism in the United States">Hinduism</a> (1%)</div><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r981673959"><div class="legend"><span class="legend-color mw-no-invert" style="background-color:#FDBF6F; color:;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Asian_Related_Religion&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="East Asian Related Religion (page does not exist)">East Asian Related Religion</a> (2%)</div>
</div>
</div></div>
<p>Major religious affiliations of the people of Colorado as of 2014 were 64% Christian, of whom there are 44% Protestant, 16% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in the United States">Roman Catholic</a>, 3% <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">Mormon</a>, and 1% <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Other religious breakdowns according to the Pew Research Center were 1% <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, 1% <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, 1% <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a> and 4% other. <a href="/wiki/Secularity" title="Secularity">Secular</a> Coloradans made up 29% of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, according to the Public Religion Research Institute, Christianity was 66% of the population. Judaism was also reported to have increased in this separate study, forming 2% of the religious landscape, while the religiously unaffiliated were reported to form 28% of the population in this separate study.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> In 2022, the same organization reported 61% was Christian (39% Protestant, 19% Catholic, 2% <a href="/wiki/Mormons" title="Mormons">Mormon</a>, 1% <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodox</a>), 2% <a href="/wiki/New_Age" title="New Age">New Age</a>, 1% Jewish, 1% Hindu, and 34% religiously unaffiliated.
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Religion_Data_Archives" title="Association of Religion Data Archives">Association of Religion Data Archives</a>, the largest Christian denominations by the number of adherents in 2010 were the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> with 811,630; multi-denominational Evangelical Protestants with 229,981; and <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> with 151,433.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> In 2020, the Association of Religion Data Archives determined the largest Christian denominations were Catholics (873,236), non/multi/inter-denominational Protestants (406,798), and Mormons (150,509).<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Throughout its non-Christian population, there were 12,500 <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_the_United_States" title="Hinduism in the United States">Hindus</a>, 7,101 <a href="/wiki/Yoga" title="Yoga">Hindu Yogis</a>, and 17,369 <a href="/wiki/Buddhism_in_the_United_States" title="Buddhism in the United States">Buddhists</a> at the 2020 study.
</p><p>Our Lady of Guadalupe Catholic Church was the first permanent Catholic parish in modern-day Colorado and was constructed by Spanish colonists from New Mexico in modern-day <a href="/wiki/Conejos,_Colorado" title="Conejos, Colorado">Conejos</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Latin_Church" title="Latin Church">Latin Church</a> Catholics are served by three dioceses: the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Denver" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Denver">Archdiocese of Denver</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Colorado_Springs" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Colorado Springs">Dioceses of Colorado Springs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Pueblo" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Pueblo">Pueblo</a>.
</p><p>The first permanent settlement by members of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_in_Colorado" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Colorado">the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Colorado</a> arrived from Mississippi and initially camped along the Arkansas River just east of the present-day site of Pueblo.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Health">Health</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Colorado is generally considered among the healthiest states by behavioral and healthcare researchers. Among the positive contributing factors is the state's well-known outdoor recreation opportunities and initiatives.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> However, there is a stratification of health metrics with wealthier counties such as <a href="/wiki/Douglas_County,_Colorado" title="Douglas County, Colorado">Douglas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pitkin_County,_Colorado" title="Pitkin County, Colorado">Pitkin</a> performing significantly better relative to southern, less wealthy counties such as <a href="/wiki/Huerfano_County,_Colorado" title="Huerfano County, Colorado">Huerfano</a> and <a href="/wiki/Las_Animas_County,_Colorado" title="Las Animas County, Colorado">Las Animas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Obesity">Obesity</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Obesity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to several studies, Coloradans have the lowest rates of obesity of any state in the US.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 24% of the population was considered medically obese, and while the lowest in the nation, the percentage had increased from 17% in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Life_expectancy">Life expectancy</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Life expectancy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to a report in the <a href="/wiki/Journal_of_the_American_Medical_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Journal of the American Medical Association">Journal of the American Medical Association</a>, residents of Colorado had a 2014 <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">life expectancy</a> of 80.21 years, the longest of any U.S. state.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Homelessness">Homelessness</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Homelessness"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="United States Department of Housing and Urban Development">HUD</a>'s 2022 <a href="/wiki/Annual_Homeless_Assessment_Report_to_Congress" title="Annual Homeless Assessment Report to Congress">Annual Homeless Assessment Report</a>, there were an estimated 10,397 <a href="/wiki/Homelessness_in_Colorado" title="Homelessness in Colorado">homeless people in Colorado</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Colorado" title="Economy of Colorado">Economy of Colorado</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG/170px-Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG/255px-Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG/340px-Denver_CO_DT_WTC_AMH_322.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a><figcaption>Denver Energy Center lies in the Denver financial district along 17th Street, known as the "<a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_of_the_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Wall Street of the West">Wall Street of the West</a>"</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg/220px-Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg/330px-Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg/440px-Corn_production_in_Colorado.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2700" data-file-height="1856" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">Corn</a> growing in <a href="/wiki/Larimer_County,_Colorado" title="Larimer County, Colorado">Larimer County</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2019 the total employment was 2,473,192. The number of employer establishments is 174,258.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The total state product in 2015 was $318.6 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Median Annual Household Income in 2016 was $70,666, 8th in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._states_by_GDP_per_capita_(nominal)" class="mw-redirect" title="List of U.S. states by GDP per capita (nominal)">Per capita personal income</a> in 2010 was $51,940, ranking Colorado 11th in the nation.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> The state's economy broadened from its mid-19th-century roots in mining when irrigated agriculture developed, and by the late 19th century, raising livestock had become important. Early industry was based on the extraction and processing of minerals and agricultural products. Current agricultural products are cattle, wheat, <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy products</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">corn</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hay" title="Hay">hay</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Federal_government_of_the_United_States" title="Federal government of the United States">federal government</a> operates several federal facilities in the state, including <a href="/wiki/NORAD" title="NORAD">NORAD</a> (North American Aerospace Defense Command), <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a>, Schriever Air Force Base located approximately 10 miles (16 kilometers) east of <a href="/wiki/Peterson_Air_Force_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Peterson Air Force Base">Peterson Air Force Base</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Carson" title="Fort Carson">Fort Carson</a>, both located in <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs,_Colorado" title="Colorado Springs, Colorado">Colorado Springs</a> within El Paso County; <a href="/wiki/NOAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>, the National Renewable Energy Laboratory (<a href="/wiki/NREL" class="mw-redirect" title="NREL">NREL</a>) in Golden, and the <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Standards_and_Technology" title="National Institute of Standards and Technology">National Institute of Standards and Technology</a> in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>; <a href="/wiki/U.S._Geological_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Geological Survey">U.S. Geological Survey</a> and other government agencies at the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Federal_Center" title="Denver Federal Center">Denver Federal Center</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lakewood,_Colorado" title="Lakewood, Colorado">Lakewood</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Mint" title="Denver Mint">Denver Mint</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buckley_Space_Force_Base" title="Buckley Space Force Base">Buckley Space Force Base</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Tenth_Circuit" title="United States Court of Appeals for the Tenth Circuit">Tenth Circuit Court of Appeals</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Byron_G._Rogers_Federal_Building_and_United_States_Courthouse" title="Byron G. Rogers Federal Building and United States Courthouse">Byron G. Rogers Federal Building and United States Courthouse</a> in Denver; and a federal <a href="/wiki/ADX_Florence" title="ADX Florence">Supermax Prison</a> and other federal prisons near <a href="/wiki/Ca%C3%B1on_City,_Colorado" title="Cañon City, Colorado">Cañon City</a>. In addition to these and other <a href="/wiki/Independent_Agencies_of_the_United_States_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent Agencies of the United States Government">federal agencies</a>, Colorado has abundant <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Forest" class="mw-redirect" title="United States National Forest">National Forest</a> land and four <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Parks_of_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="List of National Parks of the United States">National Parks</a> that contribute to federal ownership of 24,615,788 acres (99,617&#160;km<sup>2</sup>) of land in Colorado, or 37% of the total area of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the second half of the 20th century, the industrial and service sectors expanded greatly. The state's economy is diversified and is notable for its concentration on scientific research and high-technology industries. Other industries include <a href="/wiki/Food_processing" title="Food processing">food processing</a>, transportation equipment, <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">machinery</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chemical_engineering" title="Chemical engineering">chemical products</a>, the extraction of metals such as gold (see <a href="/wiki/Gold_mining_in_Colorado" title="Gold mining in Colorado">Gold mining in Colorado</a>), silver, and <a href="/wiki/Molybdenum" title="Molybdenum">molybdenum</a>. Colorado now also has the largest annual production of beer in any state.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Denver is an important financial center.
</p><p>The state's diverse <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Colorado" title="Geography of Colorado">geography</a> and majestic mountains attract millions of tourists every year, including 85.2&#160;million in 2018. Tourism contributes greatly to Colorado's economy, with tourists generating $22.3 billion in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several nationally known brand names have originated in Colorado factories and laboratories. From <a href="/wiki/Denver#Economy" title="Denver">Denver</a> came the forerunner of telecommunications giant <a href="/wiki/Qwest_Corporation" title="Qwest Corporation">Qwest</a> in 1879, <a href="/wiki/Samsonite" title="Samsonite">Samsonite</a> luggage in 1910, <a href="/wiki/Gates_Corporation" title="Gates Corporation">Gates</a> belts and hoses in 1911, and <a href="/wiki/Russell_Stover_Candies" title="Russell Stover Candies">Russell Stover Candies</a> in 1923. Kuner canned vegetables began in <a href="/wiki/Brighton,_Colorado" title="Brighton, Colorado">Brighton</a> in 1864. From <a href="/wiki/Golden,_Colorado" title="Golden, Colorado">Golden</a> came <a href="/wiki/Coors_Brewing_Company" title="Coors Brewing Company">Coors</a> beer in 1873, <a href="/wiki/CoorsTek" title="CoorsTek">CoorsTek</a> industrial ceramics in 1920, and <a href="/wiki/Jolly_Rancher" title="Jolly Rancher">Jolly Rancher</a> candy in 1949. <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Fuel_and_Iron" title="Colorado Fuel and Iron">CF&amp;I</a> railroad rails, wire, nails, and pipe debuted in <a href="/wiki/Pueblo,_Colorado" title="Pueblo, Colorado">Pueblo</a> in 1892. <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Sugar" title="Imperial Sugar">Holly Sugar</a> was first milled from beets in <a href="/wiki/Holly,_Colorado" title="Holly, Colorado">Holly</a> in 1905, and later moved its headquarters to Colorado Springs. The present-day <a href="/wiki/Swift_%26_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Swift &amp; Company">Swift</a> packed meat of <a href="/wiki/Greeley,_Colorado" title="Greeley, Colorado">Greeley</a> evolved from Monfort of Colorado, Inc., established in 1930. <a href="/wiki/Estes_Industries" title="Estes Industries">Estes</a> model rockets were launched in <a href="/wiki/Penrose,_Colorado" title="Penrose, Colorado">Penrose</a> in 1958. <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins,_Colorado" title="Fort Collins, Colorado">Fort Collins</a> has been the home of <a href="/wiki/Woodward_Governor_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Woodward Governor Company">Woodward Governor Company</a>'s motor controllers (governors) since 1870, and <a href="/wiki/Oral_irrigator" title="Oral irrigator">Waterpik</a> dental water jets and showerheads since 1962. <a href="/wiki/Celestial_Seasonings" title="Celestial Seasonings">Celestial Seasonings</a> herbal teas have been made in <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a> since 1969. <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Chocolate_Factory" class="mw-redirect" title="Rocky Mountain Chocolate Factory">Rocky Mountain Chocolate Factory</a> made its first candy in <a href="/wiki/Durango,_Colorado" title="Durango, Colorado">Durango</a> in 1981.
</p><p>Colorado has a flat 4.63% <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, regardless of income level. On 3 November 2020 voters authorized an initiative to lower that income tax rate to 4.55 percent. Unlike most states, which calculate taxes based on federal <i>adjusted gross income</i>, Colorado taxes are based on <i>taxable income</i>—income after federal exemptions and federal itemized (or standard) deductions.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> Colorado's state <a href="/wiki/Sales_tax" title="Sales tax">sales tax</a> is 2.9% on retail sales. When state revenues exceed state constitutional limits, according to Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Taxpayer_Bill_of_Rights" title="Taxpayer Bill of Rights">Taxpayer Bill of Rights</a> legislation, full-year Colorado residents can claim a sales tax refund on their individual state income tax return. Many counties and cities charge their own rates, in addition to the base state rate. There are also certain county and special district taxes that may apply.
</p><p>Real estate and personal business property are taxable in Colorado. The state's senior property tax exemption was temporarily suspended by the Colorado Legislature in 2003. The tax break was scheduled to return for the assessment year 2006, payable in 2007.
</p><p>As of December&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the state's unemployment rate was 4.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The West Virginia teachers' strike in 2018 inspired <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_education_workers%27_strikes_in_the_United_States" class="mw-redirect" title="2018–19 education workers&#39; strikes in the United States">teachers in other states</a>, including <a href="/wiki/2018_Colorado_teachers%27_strike" title="2018 Colorado teachers&#39; strike">Colorado</a>, to take similar action.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Agriculture">Agriculture</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Agriculture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Corn" class="mw-redirect" title="Corn">Corn</a> is grown in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Plains" title="Eastern Plains">Eastern Plains</a> of Colorado. Arid conditions and drought negatively impacted yields in 2020<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> and 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Natural_resources">Natural resources</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Natural resources"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG/220px-Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG/330px-Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG/440px-Grand_Junction_Trip_92007_131.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a><figcaption>An <a href="/wiki/Oil_well" title="Oil well">oil well</a> in western Colorado</figcaption></figure>
<p>Colorado has significant <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon" title="Hydrocarbon">hydrocarbon</a> resources. According to the <a href="/wiki/Energy_Information_Administration" title="Energy Information Administration">Energy Information Administration</a>, Colorado hosts seven of the largest natural gas fields in the United States, and two of the largest <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil field">oil fields</a>. Conventional and unconventional natural gas output from several Colorado basins typically accounts for more than five percent of annual U.S. natural gas production. Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a> deposits hold an estimated 1 trillion barrels (160&#160;km<sup>3</sup>) of oil—nearly as much oil as the entire world's proven oil reserves.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Substantial deposits of <a href="/wiki/Bituminous_coal" title="Bituminous coal">bituminous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sub-bituminous_coal" title="Sub-bituminous coal">subbituminous</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lignite" title="Lignite">lignite</a> coal are found in the state.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Uranium_mining_in_Colorado" title="Uranium mining in Colorado">Uranium mining in Colorado</a> goes back to 1872, when pitchblende ore was taken from gold mines near Central City, Colorado. Not counting byproduct uranium from <a href="/wiki/Phosphate" title="Phosphate">phosphate</a>, Colorado is considered to have the third-largest uranium reserves of any U.S. state, behind Wyoming and New Mexico. When Colorado and Utah dominated <a href="/wiki/Radium" title="Radium">radium</a> mining from 1910 to 1922, uranium and <a href="/wiki/Vanadium" title="Vanadium">vanadium</a> were the byproducts (giving towns like present-day <a href="/wiki/Superfund_site" class="mw-redirect" title="Superfund site">Superfund site</a> <a href="/wiki/Uravan,_Colorado" title="Uravan, Colorado">Uravan</a> their names).<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Uranium price increases from 2001 to 2007 prompted several companies to revive uranium mining in Colorado. During the 1940s certain communities–including <a href="/wiki/Naturita,_Colorado" title="Naturita, Colorado">Naturita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paradox,_Colorado" title="Paradox, Colorado">Paradox</a>–earned the moniker of "<a href="/wiki/Yellowcake" title="Yellowcake">yellowcake</a> towns" from their relationship with uranium mining. Price drops and financing problems in late 2008 forced these companies to cancel or scale back the uranium-mining project. As of 2016, there were no major uranium mining operations in the state, though plans existed to restart production.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Electricity_generation">Electricity generation</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Electricity generation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_power_stations_in_Colorado" title="List of power stations in Colorado">List of power stations in Colorado</a></div>
<p>Colorado's high Rocky Mountain ridges and eastern plains offer <a href="/wiki/Wind_power_in_Colorado" title="Wind power in Colorado">wind power</a> potential, and geologic activity in the mountain areas provides the potential for <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy_in_the_United_States" title="Geothermal energy in the United States">geothermal power</a> development. Much of the state is sunny and could produce <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_Colorado" title="Solar power in Colorado">solar power</a>. Major rivers flowing from the Rocky Mountains offer <a href="/wiki/List_of_dams_and_reservoirs_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of dams and reservoirs in Colorado">hydroelectric power</a> resources.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg/220px-HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg/330px-HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg/440px-HistoryColoradoCenter1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/History_Colorado_Center" title="History Colorado Center">History Colorado Center</a> in Denver</figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Arts_and_film">Arts and film</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Arts and film"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/List_of_museums_in_Colorado" title="List of museums in Colorado">List of museums in Colorado</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_theaters_in_Colorado" title="List of theaters in Colorado">List of theaters in Colorado</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Music_of_Colorado" title="Music of Colorado">Music of Colorado</a></li></ul>
<p>Several film productions have been shot on location in Colorado, especially prominent <a href="/wiki/Western_(genre)" title="Western (genre)">Westerns</a> like <i><a href="/wiki/True_Grit_(1969_film)" title="True Grit (1969 film)">True Grit</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Searchers_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Searchers (film)">The Searchers</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/City_Slickers" title="City Slickers">City Slickers</a>,</i> <i><a href="/wiki/Butch_Cassidy_and_the_Sundance_Kid" title="Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid">Butch Cassidy and the Sundance Kid</a>, and <a href="/wiki/My_Life_with_the_Walter_Boys" title="My Life with the Walter Boys">My Life With the Walter Boys</a></i>. Several historic military forts, railways with trains still operating, and mining <a href="/wiki/List_of_ghost_towns_in_Colorado" title="List of ghost towns in Colorado">ghost towns</a> have been used and transformed for historical accuracy in well-known films. There are also several scenic highways and mountain passes that helped to feature the open road in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Vanishing_Point_(1971_film)" title="Vanishing Point (1971 film)">Vanishing Point</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bingo_(1991_film)" title="Bingo (1991 film)">Bingo</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Starman_(film)" title="Starman (film)">Starman</a></i>. Some Colorado landmarks have been featured in films, such as <a href="/wiki/The_Stanley_Hotel" title="The Stanley Hotel">The Stanley Hotel</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Dumb_and_Dumber" title="Dumb and Dumber">Dumb and Dumber</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shining_(miniseries)" title="The Shining (miniseries)">The Shining</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Sculptured_House" title="Sculptured House">Sculptured House</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Sleeper_(1973_film)" title="Sleeper (1973 film)">Sleeper</a></i>. In 2015, <i><a href="/wiki/Furious_7" title="Furious 7">Furious 7</a></i> was to film driving sequences on <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak_Highway" title="Pikes Peak Highway">Pikes Peak Highway</a> in Colorado. The TV adult-animated series <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park" title="South Park">South Park</a></i> takes place in central Colorado in the titular town. Additionally, The TV series <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Luck_Charlie" title="Good Luck Charlie">Good Luck Charlie</a></i> was set, but not filmed, in Denver, Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The Colorado Office of Film and Television has noted that more than 400 films have been shot in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also several established film festivals in Colorado, including <a href="/wiki/Aspen_Shortsfest" title="Aspen Shortsfest">Aspen Shortsfest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boulder_International_Film_Festival" title="Boulder International Film Festival">Boulder International Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Castle_Rock_Film_Festival" title="Castle Rock Film Festival">Castle Rock Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Denver_Film_Festival" title="Denver Film Festival">Denver Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Festivus_Film_Festival" title="Festivus Film Festival">Festivus Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mile_High_Horror_Film_Festival" title="Mile High Horror Film Festival">Mile High Horror Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moondance_International_Film_Festival" title="Moondance International Film Festival">Moondance International Film Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mountainfilm_in_Telluride" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountainfilm in Telluride">Mountainfilm in Telluride</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Women%27s_Film_Festival" title="Rocky Mountain Women&#39;s Film Festival">Rocky Mountain Women's Film Festival</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Telluride_Film_Festival" title="Telluride Film Festival">Telluride Film Festival</a>.
</p><p>Many notable writers have lived or spent extended periods in Colorado. <a href="/wiki/Beat_Generation" title="Beat Generation">Beat Generation</a> writers <a href="/wiki/Jack_Kerouac" title="Jack Kerouac">Jack Kerouac</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neal_Cassady" title="Neal Cassady">Neal Cassady</a> lived in and around Denver for several years each.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> Irish playwright <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Wilde" title="Oscar Wilde">Oscar Wilde</a> visited Colorado on his tour of the United States in 1882, writing in his 1906 <i>Impressions of America</i> that <a href="/wiki/Leadville,_Colorado" title="Leadville, Colorado">Leadville</a> was "the richest city in the world.  It has also got the reputation of being the roughest, and every man carries a <a href="/wiki/Revolver" title="Revolver">revolver</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cuisine">Cuisine</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Cuisine"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Colorado is known for its <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_the_Southwestern_United_States" title="Cuisine of the Southwestern United States">Southwest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_cuisine" title="Rocky Mountain cuisine">Rocky Mountain cuisine</a>, with Mexican restaurants found throughout the state.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a> was named America's Foodiest Town 2010 by <a href="/wiki/Bon_App%C3%A9tit" title="Bon Appétit">Bon Appétit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bon_Appétit_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bon_Appétit-187">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Boulder, and Colorado in general, is home to several national food and beverage companies, top-tier restaurants and farmers' markets. Boulder also has more Master <a href="/wiki/Sommelier" title="Sommelier">Sommeliers</a> per capita than any other city, including San Francisco and New York.<sup id="cite_ref-Denver_Magazine_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Denver_Magazine-188">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">Denver</a> is known for steak, but now has a diverse culinary scene with many restaurants.<sup id="cite_ref-Travel_+_Leisure_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Travel_+_Leisure-189">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Polidori_Sausage" title="Polidori Sausage">Polidori Sausage</a> is a brand of pork products available in supermarkets, which originated in Colorado, in the early 20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Food_%26_Wine_Classic" class="mw-redirect" title="Food &amp; Wine Classic">Food &amp; Wine Classic</a> is held annually each June in <a href="/wiki/Aspen,_Colorado" title="Aspen, Colorado">Aspen</a>. Aspen also has a reputation as the culinary capital of the Rocky Mountain region.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Wine_and_beer">Wine and beer</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Wine and beer"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Colorado_wine" title="Colorado wine">Colorado wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colorado_beer" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado beer">Colorado beer</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Colorado_wine" title="Colorado wine">Colorado wines</a> include award-winning varietals that have attracted favorable notice from outside the state.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> With wines made from traditional <i><a href="/wiki/Vitis_vinifera" title="Vitis vinifera">Vitis vinifera</a></i> grapes along with wines made from cherries, peaches, plums, and honey, Colorado wines have won top national and international awards for their quality.<sup id="cite_ref-Jefferson_Cup_Invitational_Wine_Competition_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jefferson_Cup_Invitational_Wine_Competition-193">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Colorado's grape growing regions contain the highest elevation <a href="/wiki/Vineyard" title="Vineyard">vineyards</a> in the United States,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> with most <a href="/wiki/Viticulture" title="Viticulture">viticulture</a> in the state practiced between 4,000 and 7,000 feet (1,219 and 2,134&#160;m) <a href="/wiki/Above_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above sea level">above sea level</a>. The mountain <a href="/wiki/Climate" title="Climate">climate</a> ensures warm summer days and cool nights. Colorado is home to two designated <a href="/wiki/American_Viticultural_Area" title="American Viticultural Area">American Viticultural Areas</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Valley_AVA" title="Grand Valley AVA">Grand Valley AVA</a> and the <a href="/wiki/West_Elks_AVA" title="West Elks AVA">West Elks AVA</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Alcohol_and_Tobacco_Tax_and_Trade_Bureau_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Alcohol_and_Tobacco_Tax_and_Trade_Bureau-195">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> where most of the vineyards in the state are located. However, an increasing number of wineries are located along the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Colorado_Wine_Industry_Development_Board_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Colorado_Wine_Industry_Development_Board-196">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, <a href="/wiki/Wine_Enthusiast_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="Wine Enthusiast Magazine">Wine Enthusiast Magazine</a> named Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Grand_Valley_AVA" title="Grand Valley AVA">Grand Valley AVA</a> in Mesa County, Colorado, as one of the Top Ten wine travel destinations in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Colorado is home to many nationally praised <a href="/wiki/Microbreweries" class="mw-redirect" title="Microbreweries">microbreweries</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/New_Belgium_Brewing_Company" title="New Belgium Brewing Company">New Belgium Brewing Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Odell_Brewing_Company" title="Odell Brewing Company">Odell Brewing Company</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Divide_Brewing_Company" title="Great Divide Brewing Company">Great Divide Brewing Company</a>, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bristol_Brewing_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bristol Brewing Company (page does not exist)">Bristol Brewing Company</a>. The area of northern Colorado near and between the cities of Denver, <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Collins">Fort Collins</a> is known as the "Napa Valley of Beer" due to its high density of <a href="/wiki/Craft_breweries" class="mw-redirect" title="Craft breweries">craft breweries</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Denver_Beer_Triangle_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Denver_Beer_Triangle-199">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Marijuana_and_hemp">Marijuana and hemp</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Marijuana and hemp"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Colorado is open to <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> (marijuana) <a href="/wiki/Recreational_drug_use" title="Recreational drug use">tourism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> With the adoption of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Amendment_64" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado Amendment 64">64th state amendment</a> in 2012, Colorado became the first state in the union to <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cannabis_by_U.S._jurisdiction" title="Legality of cannabis by U.S. jurisdiction">legalize marijuana</a> for <a href="/wiki/Medical_cannabis_in_the_United_States#Colorado" title="Medical cannabis in the United States">medicinal</a> (2000), industrial (referring to <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">hemp</a>, 2012), and <a href="/wiki/2012_Colorado_Amendment_64" title="2012 Colorado Amendment 64">recreational</a> (2012) use. Colorado's marijuana industry sold $1.31&#160;billion worth of marijuana in 2016 and $1.26&#160;billion in the first three-quarters of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The state generated tax, fee, and license revenue of $194&#160;million in 2016 on legal marijuana sales.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Colorado regulates hemp as any part of the plant with less than 0.3% THC.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 4, 2014, Senate Bill 14–184 addressing oversight of Colorado's industrial hemp program was first introduced, ultimately being signed into law by Governor John Hickenlooper on May 31, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Medicinal_use">Medicinal use</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Medicinal use"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On November 7, 2000, 54% of Colorado voters passed Amendment 20, which amends the Colorado State constitution to allow the <a href="/wiki/Medical_use_of_cannabis" class="mw-redirect" title="Medical use of cannabis">medical use of marijuana</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-norml-co_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-norml-co-205">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> A patient's medical use of marijuana, within the following limits, is lawful:
</p>
<ul><li>(I) No more than 2 ounces (57&#160;g) of a usable form of marijuana; and</li>
<li>(II) No more than twelve marijuana plants, with six or fewer being mature, flowering plants that are producing a usable form of marijuana.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Currently, Colorado has listed "eight medical conditions for which patients can use marijuana—cancer, glaucoma, HIV/AIDS, muscle spasms, seizures, severe pain, severe nausea and cachexia, or dramatic weight loss and muscle atrophy".<sup id="cite_ref-Young_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Young-207">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> While governor, <a href="/wiki/John_Hickenlooper" title="John Hickenlooper">John Hickenlooper</a> allocated about half of the state's $13&#160;million "Medical Marijuana Program Cash Fund"<sup id="cite_ref-MMPCF_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MMPCF-208">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> to medical research in the 2014 budget.<sup id="cite_ref-Markus_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Markus-209">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> By 2018, the Medical Marijuana Program Cash Fund was the "largest pool of pot money in the state" and was used to fund programs including research into pediatric applications for controlling autism symptoms.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Recreational_use">Recreational use</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Recreational use"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On November 6, 2012, voters amended the state constitution to protect "personal use" of marijuana for adults, establishing a framework to regulate marijuana in a manner similar to <a href="/wiki/Alcohol_(drug)" title="Alcohol (drug)">alcohol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> The first recreational marijuana shops in Colorado, and by extension the United States, opened their doors on January 1, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Healy_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Healy-212">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_Colorado" title="Transportation in Colorado">Transportation in Colorado</a></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70,_entering_from_Utah_(2006).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70%2C_entering_from_Utah_%282006%29.jpg/220px-%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70%2C_entering_from_Utah_%282006%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70%2C_entering_from_Utah_%282006%29.jpg/330px-%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70%2C_entering_from_Utah_%282006%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70%2C_entering_from_Utah_%282006%29.jpg/440px-%22Welcome_to_Colorful_Colorado%22_state_welcome_sign_along_Interstate_70%2C_entering_from_Utah_%282006%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1730" data-file-height="1235" /></a><figcaption>A Colorado state welcome sign</figcaption></figure>
<p>Colorado's primary mode of transportation (in terms of passengers) is its highway system. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_25_in_Colorado" title="Interstate 25 in Colorado">Interstate&#160;25</a> (I-25) is the primary north–south highway in the state, connecting Pueblo, Colorado Springs, Denver, and Fort Collins, and extending north to Wyoming and south to New Mexico. <a href="/wiki/Interstate_70_in_Colorado" title="Interstate 70 in Colorado">I-70</a> is the primary east–west corridor. It connects Grand Junction and the mountain communities with Denver and enters Utah and Kansas. The state is home to a network of US and Colorado highways that provide access to all principal areas of the state. Many smaller communities are connected to this network only via county roads.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Denver_International_Airport.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/220px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/330px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Denver_International_Airport.jpg/440px-Denver_International_Airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a><figcaption>The main terminal of Denver International Airport evokes the peaks of the <a href="/wiki/Front_Range" title="Front Range">Front Range</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Denver_International_Airport" title="Denver International Airport">Denver International Airport</a> (DIA) is the third-busiest domestic U.S. and <a href="/wiki/World%27s_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s busiest airports by passenger traffic">international airport in the world by passenger traffic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> DIA handles by far the largest volume of commercial air traffic in Colorado and is the busiest U.S. hub airport between Chicago and the Pacific coast, making Denver the most important airport for connecting passenger traffic in the western United States.
</p><p>Public transportation bus services are offered both intra-city and inter-city—including the Denver metro area's RTD services. The <a href="/wiki/Regional_Transportation_District" title="Regional Transportation District">Regional Transportation District</a> (RTD) operates the popular <a href="/wiki/RTD_Bus_%26_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="RTD Bus &amp; Rail">RTD Bus &amp; Rail</a> transit system in the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver Metropolitan Area">Denver Metropolitan Area</a>. As of January&#160;2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the RTD rail system had 170 light-rail vehicles, serving 47 miles (76&#160;km) of track. In addition to local public transit, intercity bus service is provided by <a href="/wiki/Burlington_Trailways" title="Burlington Trailways">Burlington Trailways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bustang" title="Bustang">Bustang</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Express_Arrow&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Express Arrow (page does not exist)">Express Arrow</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Greyhound_Lines" title="Greyhound Lines">Greyhound Lines</a>.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg/220px-California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg/330px-California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg/440px-California_Zephyr--Eastbound_meets_Westbound_in_Glenwood_Canyon.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a><figcaption>The westbound and eastbound <i><a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyrs</a></i> meet in the <a href="/wiki/Glenwood_Canyon" title="Glenwood Canyon">Glenwood Canyon</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Amtrak" title="Amtrak">Amtrak</a> operates two passenger rail lines in Colorado, the <i><a href="/wiki/California_Zephyr" title="California Zephyr">California Zephyr</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Southwest_Chief" title="Southwest Chief">Southwest Chief</a></i>. Colorado's contribution to world railroad history was forged principally by the <a href="/wiki/Denver_and_Rio_Grande_Western_Railroad" title="Denver and Rio Grande Western Railroad">Denver and Rio Grande Western Railroad</a> which began in 1870 and wrote the book on mountain railroading. In 1988 the "Rio Grande" was acquired, but was merged into, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Pacific_Railroad" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Pacific Railroad">Southern Pacific Railroad</a> by their joint owner <a href="/wiki/Philip_Anschutz" title="Philip Anschutz">Philip Anschutz</a>. On September 11, 1996, Anschutz sold the combined company to the <a href="/wiki/Union_Pacific_Railroad" title="Union Pacific Railroad">Union Pacific Railroad</a>, creating the largest railroad network in the United States. The Anschutz sale was partly in response to the earlier merger of Burlington Northern and Santa Fe which formed the large Burlington Northern and Santa Fe Railway (BNSF), Union Pacific's principal competitor in western U.S. railroading. Both Union Pacific and BNSF have extensive freight operations in Colorado.
</p><p>Colorado's freight railroad network consists of 2,688 miles of Class I trackage. It is integral to the U.S. economy, being a critical artery for the movement of energy, agriculture, mining, and industrial commodities as well as general freight and manufactured products between the East and Midwest and the Pacific coast states.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In August 2014, Colorado began to issue driver licenses to <a href="/wiki/Alien_(law)" title="Alien (law)">aliens</a> <a href="/wiki/Illegal_immigration_to_the_United_States" title="Illegal immigration to the United States">not lawfully in the United States</a> who lived in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> In September 2014, <a href="/wiki/KCNC" class="mw-redirect" title="KCNC">KCNC</a> reported that 524 non-citizens were issued Colorado driver licenses that are normally issued to U.S. citizens living in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Education">Education</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Education"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_colleges_and_universities_in_Colorado" title="List of colleges and universities in Colorado">List of colleges and universities in Colorado</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Table_of_Colorado_school_districts" class="mw-redirect" title="Table of Colorado school districts">Table of Colorado school districts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Table_of_Colorado_charter_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Table of Colorado charter schools">Table of Colorado charter schools</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Auraria_Campus" title="Auraria Campus">Auraria Campus</a></div>
<p>The first institution of <a href="/wiki/Higher_education_in_the_United_States" title="Higher education in the United States">higher education</a> in the Colorado Territory was the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Seminary" class="mw-redirect" title="Colorado Seminary">Colorado Seminary</a>, opened on November 16, 1864, by the <a href="/wiki/Methodist_Episcopal_Church" title="Methodist Episcopal Church">Methodist Episcopal Church</a>. The seminary closed in 1867 but reopened in 1880 as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a>. In 1870, the Bishop <a href="/wiki/George_M._Randall_(bishop)" title="George M. Randall (bishop)">George Maxwell Randall</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Church_(United_States)" title="Episcopal Church (United States)">Episcopal Church</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Episcopal_Diocese_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Episcopal Diocese of Colorado">Missionary District of Colorado and Parts Adjacent</a> opened the first of what become the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_University_Schools" title="Colorado University Schools">Colorado University Schools</a> which would include the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_School_of_Mines" title="Colorado School of Mines">Territorial School of Mines</a> opened in 1873 and sold to the Colorado Territory in 1874. These schools were initially run by the Episcopal Church.<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> An 1861 territorial act called for the creation of a public university in Boulder, though it would not be until 1876 that the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Colorado_Boulder" title="University of Colorado Boulder">University of Colorado</a> was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The 1876 act also renamed Territorial School of Mines as the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_School_of_Mines" title="Colorado School of Mines">Colorado School of Mines</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> An 1870 territorial act created the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Agricultural College of Colorado</a> which opened in 1879.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The college was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State College of Agriculture and Mechanic Arts</a> in 1935, and became <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a> in 1957.
</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/List_of_Catholic_universities_and_colleges_in_the_United_States" title="List of Catholic universities and colleges in the United States">Catholic college</a> in Colorado was the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> Sacred Heart College, which was founded in New Mexico in 1877, moved to <a href="/wiki/Morrison,_Colorado" title="Morrison, Colorado">Morrison</a> in 1884, and to Denver in 1887. The college was renamed Regis College in 1921 and <a href="/wiki/Regis_University" title="Regis University">Regis University</a> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> On April 1, 1924, armed students patrolled the campus after a <a href="/wiki/Cross_burning" title="Cross burning">burning cross</a> was found, the climax of tensions between Regis College and the locally-powerful Ku Klux Klan.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Following a 1950 assessment by the Service Academy Board, it was determined that there was a need to supplement the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Military_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Military Academy">U.S. Military</a> and <a href="/wiki/U.S._Naval_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Naval Academy">Naval Academies</a> with a third school that would provide commissioned officers for the newly independent Air Force. On April 1, 1954, President <a href="/wiki/Dwight_Eisenhower" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwight Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a> signed a law that moved for the creation of a <a href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force_Academy" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Air Force Academy">U.S. Air Force Academy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, Colorado Springs was selected to host the new institution. From its establishment in 1955, until the construction of appropriate facilities in Colorado Springs was completed and opened in 1958, the Air Force Academy operated out of <a href="/wiki/Lowry_Air_Force_Base" title="Lowry Air Force Base">Lowry Air Force Base</a> in Denver. With the opening of the Colorado Springs facility, the cadets moved to the new campus, though not in the full-kit march that some urban and campus legends suggest.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> The first class of <a href="/wiki/United_States_Space_Force" title="United States Space Force">Space Force</a> <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officers</a> from the Air Force Academy commissioned on April 18, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Colorado" title="Government of Colorado">Government of Colorado</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="State_government">State government</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: State government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

<p>Like the federal government and all other U.S. states, Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_State_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Constitution of the State of Colorado">state constitution</a> provides for three branches of government: the legislative, the executive, and the judicial branches.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Colorado" title="Governor of Colorado">Governor of Colorado</a> heads the state's executive branch. The current governor is <a href="/wiki/Jared_Polis" title="Jared Polis">Jared Polis</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrat</a>. Colorado's other statewide elected executive officers are the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Lieutenant Governor of Colorado">Lieutenant Governor of Colorado</a> (elected on a <a href="/wiki/Ticket_(election)" title="Ticket (election)">ticket</a> with the Governor), <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_of_Colorado" title="Secretary of State of Colorado">Secretary of State of Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_Treasurer" title="Colorado State Treasurer">Colorado State Treasurer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="Attorney General of Colorado">Attorney General of Colorado</a>, all of whom serve four-year terms.
</p><p>The seven-member <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Supreme_Court" title="Colorado Supreme Court">Colorado Supreme Court</a> is the state's highest court, with seven justices. The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Court_of_Appeals" title="Colorado Court of Appeals">Colorado Court of Appeals</a>, with 22 judges, sits in divisions of three judges each. Colorado is divided into 22 judicial districts, each of which has a district court and a county court with limited jurisdiction. The state also has <a href="/wiki/Colorado_water_courts" title="Colorado water courts">specialized water courts</a>, which sit in seven distinct divisions around the state and which decide matters relating to water rights and the use and administration of water.
</p><p>The state legislative body is the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_General_Assembly" title="Colorado General Assembly">Colorado General Assembly</a>, which is made up of two houses – the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_House_of_Representatives" title="Colorado House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Senate" title="Colorado Senate">Senate</a>. The House has 65 members and the Senate has 35. As of 2023<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic Party</a> holds a 23 to 12 majority in the Senate and a 46 to 19 majority in the House.
</p><p>Most Coloradans are native to other states (nearly 60% according to the 2000 census),<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> and this is illustrated by the fact that the state did not have a native-born governor from 1975 (when <a href="/wiki/John_David_Vanderhoof" class="mw-redirect" title="John David Vanderhoof">John David Vanderhoof</a> left office) until 2007, when <a href="/wiki/Bill_Ritter" title="Bill Ritter">Bill Ritter</a> took office; <a href="/wiki/2006_Colorado_gubernatorial_election" title="2006 Colorado gubernatorial election">his election</a> the previous year marked the first electoral victory for a native-born Coloradan in a gubernatorial race since 1958 (Vanderhoof had ascended from the Lieutenant Governorship when <a href="/wiki/John_Arthur_Love" title="John Arthur Love">John Arthur Love</a> was given a position in <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">Richard Nixon</a>'s administration in 1973).
</p><p>Tax is collected by the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Department_of_Revenue" title="Colorado Department of Revenue">Colorado Department of Revenue</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Politics">Politics</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Politics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Colorado" title="Politics of Colorado">Politics of Colorado</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Political_party_strength_in_Colorado" title="Political party strength in Colorado">Political party strength in Colorado</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_elections_in_Colorado" title="United States presidential elections in Colorado">United States presidential elections in Colorado</a></div>
