<p>Colorado was once considered a <a href="/wiki/Swing_state" title="Swing state">swing state</a>, but has become a relatively safe <a href="/wiki/Red_states_and_blue_states" title="Red states and blue states">blue state</a> in both state and federal elections. In presidential elections, it had not been won until <a href="/wiki/2020_United_States_presidential_election_in_Colorado" title="2020 United States presidential election in Colorado">2020</a> by double digits since <a href="/wiki/1984_United_States_presidential_election_in_Colorado" title="1984 United States presidential election in Colorado">1984</a> and has backed the winning candidate in 9 of the last 11 elections. Coloradans have elected 17 <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democrats</a> and 12 <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republicans</a> to the governorship in the last 100 years.
</p><p>In presidential politics, Colorado was considered a reliably Republican state during the post-World War II era, voting for the Democratic candidate only in 1948, 1964, and 1992. However, it became a competitive swing state in the 1990s. Since the mid-2000s, it has swung heavily to the Democrats, voting for <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2008 and 2012, <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> in 2016, and <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> in 2020.
</p><p>Colorado politics exhibits a contrast between conservative cities such as Colorado Springs and Grand Junction, and liberal cities such as Boulder and Denver. Democrats are strongest in <a href="/wiki/Denver_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="Denver Metropolitan Area">metropolitan Denver</a>, the college towns of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Collins,_Colorado" title="Fort Collins, Colorado">Fort Collins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Boulder,_Colorado" title="Boulder, Colorado">Boulder</a>, southern Colorado (including Pueblo), and several western ski resort counties. The Republicans are strongest in the Eastern Plains, Colorado Springs, Greeley, and far Western Colorado near Grand Junction.
</p><p>Colorado is represented by two members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Senate" title="United States Senate">United States Senate</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Classes_of_United_States_Senators#Class_2" class="mw-redirect" title="Classes of United States Senators">Class 2</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Hickenlooper" title="John Hickenlooper">John Hickenlooper</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 2021</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Classes_of_United_States_Senators#Class_3" class="mw-redirect" title="Classes of United States Senators">Class 3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bennet" title="Michael Bennet">Michael Bennet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 2009</li></ul>
<p>Colorado is represented by eight members of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="United States House of Representatives">United States House of Representatives</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_1st_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 1st congressional district">1st district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Diana_DeGette" title="Diana DeGette">Diana DeGette</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 1997</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_2nd_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 2nd congressional district">2nd district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Joe_Neguse" title="Joe Neguse">Joe Neguse</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 2019</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_3rd_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 3rd congressional district">3rd district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Lauren_Boebert" title="Lauren Boebert">Lauren Boebert</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>), since 2021</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_4th_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 4th congressional district">4th district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Greg_Lopez" title="Greg Lopez">Greg Lopez</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>), since 2024</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_5th_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 5th congressional district">5th district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Doug_Lamborn" title="Doug Lamborn">Doug Lamborn</a> (<a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a>), since 2007</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_6th_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 6th congressional district">6th district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Jason_Crow" title="Jason Crow">Jason Crow</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 2019</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_7th_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 7th congressional district">7th district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Brittany_Pettersen" title="Brittany Pettersen">Brittany Pettersen</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 2023</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado%27s_8th_congressional_district" title="Colorado&#39;s 8th congressional district">8th district</a>: <a href="/wiki/Yadira_Caraveo" title="Yadira Caraveo">Yadira Caraveo</a> (<a href="/wiki/Democratic_Party_(United_States)" title="Democratic Party (United States)">Democratic</a>), since 2023</li></ul>
<p>In a 2020 study, Colorado was ranked as the seventh easiest state for citizens to vote in.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Significant_initiatives_and_legislation_enacted_in_Colorado">Significant initiatives and legislation enacted in Colorado</h4><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: Significant initiatives and legislation enacted in Colorado"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Colorado was the first state in the union to enact, by voter referendum, <a href="/wiki/1893_Colorado_women%27s_suffrage_referendum" title="1893 Colorado women&#39;s suffrage referendum">a law extending</a> <a href="/wiki/Suffrage" title="Suffrage">suffrage</a> to women. That initiative was approved by the state's voters on November 7, 1893.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the November 8, 1932, ballot, Colorado approved the <a href="/wiki/Repeal_of_Prohibition" class="mw-redirect" title="Repeal of Prohibition">repeal of alcohol prohibition</a> more than a year before the <a href="/wiki/Twenty-first_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Twenty-first Amendment to the United States Constitution">Twenty-first Amendment to the United States Constitution</a> was ratified.
</p><p>Colorado has banned, via C.R.S. section 12-6-302, the sale of motor vehicles on Sunday since at least 1953.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1972 Colorado voters rejected a <a href="/wiki/1972_Denver_Winter_Olympics_referendum" title="1972 Denver Winter Olympics referendum">referendum proposal</a> to fund the <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">1976 Winter Olympics</a>, which had been scheduled to be held in the state. Denver had been chosen by the <a href="/wiki/International_Olympic_Committee" title="International Olympic Committee">International Olympic Committee</a> as the host city on May 12, 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1992, by a margin of 53 to 47 percent, Colorado voters approved an amendment to the state constitution (Amendment 2) that would have prevented any city, town, or county in the state from taking any legislative, executive or judicial action to recognize homosexuals or bisexuals as a <a href="/wiki/Protected_class" class="mw-redirect" title="Protected class">protected class</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, in a 6–3 ruling in <i><a href="/wiki/Romer_v._Evans" title="Romer v. Evans">Romer v. Evans</a></i>, the U.S. Supreme Court found that preventing protected status based upon homosexuality or <a href="/wiki/Bisexuality" title="Bisexuality">bisexuality</a> did not satisfy the <a href="/wiki/Equal_Protection_Clause" title="Equal Protection Clause">Equal Protection Clause</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-romervevans_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-romervevans-233">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2006, voters passed <a href="/wiki/2006_Colorado_Amendment_43" title="2006 Colorado Amendment 43">Amendment 43</a>, which banned gay marriage in Colorado.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> That initiative was nullified by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">U.S. Supreme Court</a>'s 2015 decision in <i><a href="/wiki/Obergefell_v._Hodges" title="Obergefell v. Hodges">Obergefell v. Hodges</a></i>.
</p><p>In 2012, voters amended the state constitution protecting the "personal use" of marijuana for adults, establishing a framework to regulate <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">cannabis</a> like <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcohol</a>. The first recreational marijuana shops in Colorado, and by extension the United States, opened their doors on January 1, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Healy_212-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Healy-212">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 October 2019, Colorado became the first state to accept digital ID via its myColorado app.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The state-issued digital identifications will be considered valid when Real ID enforcement begins in 2025, in line with the <a href="/wiki/Real_ID_Act" title="Real ID Act">Real ID Act of 2005</a>. By November 2022 The Colorado Governor's Office of Information Technology announced that the myColorado app had over 1 million users.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 19, 2023, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Supreme_Court" title="Colorado Supreme Court">Colorado Supreme Court</a> ruled that <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> was disqualified from the <a href="/wiki/2024_United_States_presidential_election" title="2024 United States presidential election">2024 United States presidential election</a> in part due to his alleged incitement of the <a href="/wiki/January_6_United_States_Capitol_attack" title="January 6 United States Capitol attack">January 6 United States Capitol attack</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> On March 4, 2024, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Supreme_Court" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Supreme Court">United States Supreme Court</a> <a href="/wiki/Trump_v._Anderson" title="Trump v. Anderson">overruled</a> the Colorado decision.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Indigenous_People">Indigenous People</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=51" title="Edit section: Indigenous People"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG/220px-Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG/330px-Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG/440px-Southern_Ute_Tribal_Administration_Building.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5733" data-file-height="3675" /></a><figcaption>The Southern Ute Tribal Administration Building</figcaption></figure>
<dl><dd><i>See <a href="/wiki/Template:Indigenous_People_of_CO" class="mw-redirect" title="Template:Indigenous People of CO">Indigenous People of Colorado</a></i></dd></dl>
<p>The two <a href="/wiki/Indian_reservation" title="Indian reservation">Native American reservations</a> remaining in Colorado are the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ute_Indian_Reservation" title="Southern Ute Indian Reservation">Southern Ute Indian Reservation</a> (1873; <a href="/wiki/Ute_dialect" title="Ute dialect">Ute dialect</a>: <i>Kapuuta-wa Moghwachi Núuchi-u</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Ute_Mountain_Ute_Indian_Reservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ute Mountain Ute Indian Reservation">Ute Mountain Ute Indian Reservation</a> (1940; <a href="/wiki/Ute_dialect" title="Ute dialect">Ute dialect</a>: <i>Wʉgama Núuchi</i>).
</p><p>The two abolished Indian reservations in Colorado were the <a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_and_Arapaho_Tribes" title="Cheyenne and Arapaho Tribes">Cheyenne and Arapaho Indian Reservation</a> (1851–1870) and Ute Indian Reservation (1855–1873).
</p>
<div style="clear:both;" class=""></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Military_installations">Military installations</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=52" title="Edit section: Military installations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Carsongate.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Carsongate.JPG/220px-Carsongate.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Carsongate.JPG/330px-Carsongate.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Carsongate.JPG/440px-Carsongate.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Fort_Carson" title="Fort Carson">Fort Carson</a></figcaption></figure>

<p>The major <a href="/wiki/Military_installation" class="mw-redirect" title="Military installation">military installations</a> in Colorado include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Buckley_Space_Force_Base" title="Buckley Space Force Base">Buckley Space Force Base</a> (1938–)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Air_Reserve_Personnel_Center" title="Air Reserve Personnel Center">Air Reserve Personnel Center</a> (1953–)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Carson" title="Fort Carson">Fort Carson</a> (<a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">U.S. Army</a> 1942–)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pi%C3%B1on_Canyon_Maneuver_Site" title="Piñon Canyon Maneuver Site">Piñon Canyon Maneuver Site</a> (1983–)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peterson_Space_Force_Base" title="Peterson Space Force Base">Peterson Space Force Base</a> (1942–)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Cheyenne_Mountain_Space_Force_Station" title="Cheyenne Mountain Space Force Station">Cheyenne Mountain Space Force Station</a> (1961–)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Chemical_Depot" title="Pueblo Chemical Depot">Pueblo Chemical Depot</a> (U.S. Army 1942–)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Schriever_Space_Force_Base" title="Schriever Space Force Base">Schriever Space Force Base</a> (1983–)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force_Academy" title="United States Air Force Academy">United States Air Force Academy</a> (1954–)</li></ul>
<p>Former military posts in Colorado include:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_Fort_(Colorado)" title="Spanish Fort (Colorado)">Spanish Fort</a> (<a href="/wiki/Spanish_Army" title="Spanish Army">Spanish Army</a> 1819–1821)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Massachusetts_(Colorado)" title="Fort Massachusetts (Colorado)">Fort Massachusetts</a> (U.S. Army 1852–1858)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Garland" title="Fort Garland">Fort Garland</a> (U.S. Army 1858–1883)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Camp_Collins" title="Camp Collins">Camp Collins</a> (U.S. Army 1862–1870)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_Logan" title="Fort Logan">Fort Logan</a> (U.S. Army 1887–1946)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Colorado_National_Guard_Armory" title="Colorado National Guard Armory">Colorado National Guard Armory</a> (1913–1933)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fitzsimons_Army_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Fitzsimons Army Hospital">Fitzsimons Army Hospital</a> (U.S. Army 1918–1999)</li>
<li>Denver Medical Depot (U.S. Army 1925–1949)<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lowry_Air_Force_Base" title="Lowry Air Force Base">Lowry Air Force Base</a> (1938–1994)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pueblo_Army_Air_Base" class="mw-redirect" title="Pueblo Army Air Base">Pueblo Army Air Base</a> (1941–1948)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Arsenal" title="Rocky Mountain Arsenal">Rocky Mountain Arsenal</a> (U.S. Army 1942–1992)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Camp_Hale" title="Camp Hale">Camp Hale</a> (U.S. Army 1942–1945)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/La_Junta_Army_Air_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="La Junta Army Air Field">La Junta Army Air Field</a> (1942–1946)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leadville_Army_Air_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Leadville Army Air Field">Leadville Army Air Field</a> (1943–1944)</li></ul>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Protected_areas">Protected areas</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=53" title="Edit section: Protected areas"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg/220px-Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg/330px-Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg/440px-Fall05-LongsPeakCU_JPG_RSZ_md.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="973" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Longs_Peak" title="Longs Peak">Longs Peak</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_National_Park" title="Rocky Mountain National Park">Rocky Mountain National Park</a>.</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Colorado" title="List of protected areas of Colorado">List of protected areas of Colorado</a></div>
<p>Colorado is home to <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_parks_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national parks in Colorado">4 national parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_monuments_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national monuments in Colorado">9 national monuments</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_historic_sites_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national historic sites in Colorado">3 national historic sites</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_recreation_areas_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national recreation areas in Colorado">2 national recreation areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_historic_trails_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national historic trails in Colorado">4 national historic trails</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_scenic_trails_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national scenic trails in Colorado">1 national scenic trail</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_forests_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national forests in Colorado">11 national forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_grasslands_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national grasslands in Colorado">2 national grasslands</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_wildernesses_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national wildernesses in Colorado">44 national wildernesses</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_conservation_areas_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national conservation areas in Colorado">3 national conservation areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_wildlife_refuges_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national wildlife refuges in Colorado">8 national wildlife refuges</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_heritage_areas_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national heritage areas in Colorado">3 national heritage areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_historic_landmarks_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national historic landmarks in Colorado">26 national historic landmarks</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_natural_landmarks_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national natural landmarks in Colorado">16 national natural landmarks</a>, more than 1,500 <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Register_of_Historic_Places_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of National Register of Historic Places in Colorado">National Register of Historic Places</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_wild_and_scenic_rivers_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of wild and scenic rivers in Colorado">1 wild and scenic river</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Colorado_state_parks" title="List of Colorado state parks">42 state parks</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Colorado_state_wildlife_areas" title="List of Colorado state wildlife areas">307 state wildlife areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Colorado_natural_areas" title="List of Colorado natural areas">93 state natural areas</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_recreation_trails_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of national recreation trails in Colorado">28 national recreation trails</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_regional_trails_in_Colorado" class="mw-redirect" title="List of regional trails in Colorado">6 regional trails</a>, and numerous other scenic, historic, and recreational areas.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Sports">Sports</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=54" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Coors_field_1.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Coors_field_1.JPG/172px-Coors_field_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="172" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Coors_field_1.JPG/258px-Coors_field_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Coors_field_1.JPG/344px-Coors_field_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a><figcaption>The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a> baseball club at <a href="/wiki/Coors_Field" title="Coors Field">Coors Field</a></figcaption></figure>

<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pepsi_Center.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pepsi_Center.jpg/172px-Pepsi_Center.jpg" decoding="async" width="172" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pepsi_Center.jpg/258px-Pepsi_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pepsi_Center.jpg/344px-Pepsi_Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Ball_Arena" title="Ball Arena">Ball Arena</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Denver_Nuggets" title="Denver Nuggets">Denver Nuggets</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Avalanche" title="Colorado Avalanche">Colorado Avalanche</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Mammoth" title="Colorado Mammoth">Colorado Mammoth</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dick%27s_Park.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Dick%27s_Park.jpg/172px-Dick%27s_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="172" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Dick%27s_Park.jpg/258px-Dick%27s_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Dick%27s_Park.jpg/344px-Dick%27s_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Dick%27s_Sporting_Goods_Park" title="Dick&#39;s Sporting Goods Park">Dick's Sporting Goods Park</a>, home of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rapids" title="Colorado Rapids">Colorado Rapids</a></figcaption></figure>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg/172px-Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg" decoding="async" width="172" height="129" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg/258px-Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg/344px-Weidner_Field_from_Sierra_Madre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Weidner_Field" title="Weidner Field">Weidner Field</a> in Colorado Springs, home of the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs_Switchbacks_FC" title="Colorado Springs Switchbacks FC">Colorado Springs Switchbacks FC</a></figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sports_in_Colorado" title="Sports in Colorado">Sports in Colorado</a></div>
<p>Colorado has five <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">major professional sports leagues</a>, all based in the Denver metropolitan area. Colorado is the least populous state with a franchise in each of the major professional sports leagues.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Springs_Snow_Sox" title="Colorado Springs Snow Sox">Colorado Springs Snow Sox</a> professional baseball team is based in Colorado Springs. The team is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pecos_League" title="Pecos League">Pecos League</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Independent_baseball" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent baseball">independent baseball</a> league which is not affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major</a> or <a href="/wiki/Minor_League_Baseball" title="Minor League Baseball">Minor League Baseball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pikes_Peak_International_Hill_Climb" title="Pikes Peak International Hill Climb">Pikes Peak International Hill Climb</a> is a major hill climbing motor race held on the Pikes Peak Highway.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Cherry_Hills_Country_Club" title="Cherry Hills Country Club">Cherry Hills Country Club</a> has hosted several professional golf tournaments, including the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Open_(golf)" title="U.S. Open (golf)">U.S. Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Senior_Open" title="U.S. Senior Open">U.S. Senior Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/U.S._Women%27s_Open" title="U.S. Women&#39;s Open">U.S. Women's Open</a>, <a href="/wiki/PGA_Championship" title="PGA Championship">PGA Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/BMW_Championship_(PGA_Tour)" title="BMW Championship (PGA Tour)">BMW Championship</a>.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="College_athletics">College athletics</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Colorado&amp;action=edit&amp;section=56" title="Edit section: College athletics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_college_athletic_programs_in_Colorado" title="List of college athletic programs in Colorado">List of college athletic programs in Colorado</a></div>
<p>The following universities and colleges participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">National Collegiate Athletic Association</a> <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I" title="NCAA Division I">Division&#160;I</a>. The most popular college sports program is the University of Colorado Buffaloes, who used to play in the Big-12 but now play in the Pac-12. They have won the 1957 and 1991 <a href="/wiki/Orange_Bowl" title="Orange Bowl">Orange Bowl</a>, 1995 <a href="/wiki/Fiesta_Bowl" title="Fiesta Bowl">Fiesta Bowl</a>, and 1996 <a href="/wiki/Cotton_Bowl_Classic" title="Cotton Bowl Classic">Cotton Bowl Classic</a>.
</p>

<li id="cite_note-NAVD88-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NAVD88_8-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NAVD88_8-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Elevation adjusted to <a href="/wiki/North_American_Vertical_Datum_of_1988" title="North American Vertical Datum of 1988">North American Vertical Datum of 1988</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-FourCornersMonument-52"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-FourCornersMonument_52-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The official <a href="/wiki/Four_Corners_Monument" title="Four Corners Monument">Four Corners Monument</a> is located at <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">36°59'56.31608″N</a>, <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">109°2'42.62075"W</a>, 574 feet (175&#160;m) southeast of the <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">37°N</a>, <a href="/wiki/32nd_meridian_west_from_Washington" title="32nd meridian west from Washington">109°02′48″W</a> location <a href="/wiki/Thirty-sixth_United_States_Congress" class="mw-redirect" title="Thirty-sixth United States Congress">Congress</a> originally designated.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-2023_county_estimates-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-2023_county_estimates_103-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2023_county_estimates_103-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2023_county_estimates_103-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates of county population as of July 1, 2023,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As a <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Consolidated_city_and_county" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">consolidated city and county</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Denver" title="Denver">City and County  of Denver</a> is its own <a href="/wiki/County_seat#United_States" title="County seat">county seat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MuniIncCO_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MuniIncCO-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-106"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-106">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Littleton,_Colorado" title="Littleton, Colorado">Littleton, Colorado</a> also  extends into <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_County,_Colorado" title="Jefferson County, Colorado">Jefferson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_County,_Colorado" title="Douglas County, Colorado">Douglas counties</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Colorado" title="Aurora, Colorado">Aurora, Colorado</a> also extends into  <a href="/wiki/Adams_County,_Colorado" title="Adams County, Colorado">Adams</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_County,_Colorado" title="Douglas County, Colorado">Douglas  counties</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Brighton,_Colorado" title="Brighton, Colorado">Brighton, Colorado</a> also extends  into <a href="/wiki/Weld_County,_Colorado" title="Weld County, Colorado">Weld County</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-109"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-109">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Thornton,_Colorado" title="Thornton, Colorado">Thornton, Colorado</a> also extends  into <a href="/wiki/Weld_County,_Colorado" title="Weld County, Colorado">Weld County</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-110"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-110">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Highlands_Ranch,_Colorado" title="Highlands Ranch, Colorado">Highlands Ranch,  Colorado</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated place</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-111"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-111">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As a <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_in_Colorado#Consolidated_city_and_county" title="List of municipalities in Colorado">consolidated city and county</a>, the  <a href="/wiki/Broomfield,_Colorado" title="Broomfield, Colorado">City and County of Broomfield</a> is its own <a href="/wiki/County_seat#United_States" title="County seat">county seat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MuniIncCO_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MuniIncCO-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-112"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-112">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Edwards,_Colorado" title="Edwards, Colorado">Edwards, Colorado</a> is a  <a href="/wiki/Census-designated_place" title="Census-designated place">census-designated place</a>.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-2023_muni_estimates-115"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-2023_muni_estimates_115-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2023_muni_estimates_115-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2023_muni_estimates_115-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/United_States_Census_Bureau" title="United States Census Bureau">United States Census Bureau</a> estimates of municipal population as of July 1, 2022<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-120"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-120">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Persons of Hispanic or Latino origin are not distinguished between total and partial ancestry.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-242"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-242">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Air Force teams participate in other conferences, or as independents, in sports that the MW does not sponsor:
<ul><li>Boxing, a men-only sport that is not sanctioned by the NCAA, competes as an independent.</li>
<li>Fencing, a coeducational sport with men's and women's squads, also competes as an independent.</li>
<li>Men's and women's gymnastics both compete in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>.</li>
<li>Men's ice hockey competes in <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Hockey" title="Atlantic Hockey">Atlantic Hockey</a>.</li>
<li>Men's lacrosse competes in the <a href="/wiki/ASUN_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="ASUN Conference">ASUN Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Rifle, which at Air Force is a coeducational sport, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Patriot_Rifle_Conference" title="Patriot Rifle Conference">Patriot Rifle Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Men's soccer and women's swimming &amp; diving compete in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Men's wrestling competes in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>.</li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-243"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-243">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Colorado teams participate in other conferences in sports that the Pac-12 does not sponsor:
<ul><li>Men's and women's indoor track &amp; field compete in the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_Pacific_Sports_Federation" title="Mountain Pacific Sports Federation">Mountain Pacific Sports Federation</a>.</li>
<li>Skiing, a coeducational sport with men's and women's squads, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Intercollegiate_Ski_Association" title="Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association">Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association</a>.</li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-244"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-244">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Denver teams participate in other conferences in sports that The Summit League does not sponsor:
<ul><li>Women's gymnastics competes in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Men's ice hockey competes in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Hockey_Conference" title="National Collegiate Hockey Conference">National Collegiate Hockey Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Men's and women's lacrosse compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_East_Conference" title="Big East Conference">Big East Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Skiing, a coeducational sport with men's and women's squads, competes in the <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountain_Intercollegiate_Ski_Association" title="Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association">Rocky Mountain Intercollegiate Ski Association</a>.</li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-245"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-245">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Several Northern Colorado teams participate in other conferences in sports that the Big Sky does not sponsor:
<ul><li>Baseball competes in the <a href="/wiki/Summit_League" title="Summit League">Summit League</a>.</li>
<li>Women's swimming &amp; diving competes in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Athletic_Conference" title="Western Athletic Conference">Western Athletic Conference</a>.</li>
<li>Men's wrestling competes in the <a href="/wiki/Big_12_Conference" title="Big 12 Conference">Big 12 Conference</a>.</li></ul>
</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-246"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-246">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Colorado College, otherwise an <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_III" title="NCAA Division III">NCAA Division III</a> member, has two Division I teams. Men's ice hockey competes in the National Collegiate Hockey Conference and women's soccer competes in the Mountain West.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
